# Alpha Progress Log — Lando v4 Alpha (happy path coverage)

Source PRDs: spec/alpha/prd-alpha-{01..07}-*.md
Spec source of truth: spec/ROADMAP.md Phase 2 + spec/{01..19}-*.md

## Conventions

- Each story corresponds to a US-XXX section in one of the seven prd-alpha-*.md files.
  Mapping (priority -> source PRD US):
    1-8   -> prd-alpha-01-runtime-providers.md      US-001..008
    9-16  -> prd-alpha-02-service-catalog-and-app-planning.md US-009..016
    17-24 -> prd-alpha-03-tooling-and-cli-coverage.md US-017..024
    25-32 -> prd-alpha-04-recipes-and-app-initialization.md US-025..032
    28.5  -> prd-alpha-02-service-catalog-and-app-planning.md US-014b (out-of-sequence; landofile.ts loader, unblocks PRD-04 US-029)
    33-40 -> prd-alpha-05-renderer-errors-and-diagnostics.md US-033..040
    41-48 -> prd-alpha-06-persistent-caches-and-library-api.md US-041..048
    49-56 -> prd-alpha-07-ci-distribution-and-release-channel.md US-049..056

- Every story is TDD (red -> green -> clean) per the index PRD's verification contract.
- Read the corresponding source PRD section before starting a story for full acceptance criteria detail.
- Verification gate (mandatory on every story): bun run typecheck, bun run lint, bun test all green.
- Live integration tests stay gated on explicit env vars and host runtime prerequisites.

## Codebase Patterns

- Planner capability gates live in `core/src/services/planner.ts`; service-plan fields that require provider support should fail before apply with `CapabilityError` carrying service, feature, capability, provider id, and remediation.
- `meta:setup` runs at provider bootstrap through `RuntimeProviderRegistry.select()`; compiled `$bunfs` commands that bypass OCLIF need matching handlers in `core/src/cli/run.ts`.
- `provider-lando` setup state is persisted under `<userDataRoot>/providers/provider-lando/setup-state.json` when a state directory is configured.
- provider-lando live macOS machine lifecycle checks stay gated behind `LANDO_TEST_PROVIDER_LANDO_MACOS`; fake `PodmanMachineRunner` tests cover default behavior.
- Provider capability tests should force the target platform through provider factory options (for example `makeProviderLayer({ platform, ... })`) instead of relying on `process.platform` when asserting Linux vs macOS matrices.
- Provider lifecycle state should persist an encoded `AppPlan` under the provider state directory and treat stale/corrupt state as a cache miss, not a hard failure.
- App stop must preserve applied plan state for later fresh-process info/destroy commands; app destroy should remove that state after provider cleanup.
- Provider partial-apply rollback removes (force DELETE) every touched container and the app network; volumes are NEVER removed on rollback. Volume removal is `destroy(--volumes)`-only.
- Provider error `details` must be passed through `redactDetails` (see `plugins/provider-lando/src/redact.ts`) before attachment; it masks credential-named keys plus env-style `NAME=VALUE` substrings in string bodies.
- Provider errors should carry an operation-scoped name (e.g. `bringUp.network`, `bringUp.create`, `bringUp.start`) so manual cleanup can identify the exact failing API call, plus `remediation` and `cause` per spec §5.7.
- Shared `ServiceConfig` fields used by only a subset of service types (e.g. `framework`) belong on the schema as optional; per-type validation/rejection lives in `ServiceType.toServicePlan` so unrelated types ignore the field and supported types consume it. `LandofileShape` strict decoding stays intact this way.
- `ServiceTypePlanInput.appName` is the canonical seam for service types that need accurate `LANDO_APP_NAME`/`LANDO_PROJECT`; it is threaded by `AppPlanner.plan` from `landofile.name` and falls back to `basename(appRoot)` when unset.
- Beta-deferred Landofile surfaces (top-level `includes:`/`secrets:`/`env_file:`, and Landofile-level configuration expressions `${...}`/`{{ ... }}`) are rejected by `LandofileService` with `NotImplementedError` + Beta remediation BEFORE schema validation, so consumers see a tagged "defer to Beta" error instead of a generic "excess property" message. Widening this rejection set means widening the `LandofileService.discover` and (transitively) `AppPlanner.plan` error unions plus every CLI command alias (`StartAppError`, `StopAppError`, `DestroyAppError`, `InfoAppError`) that depends on them.
- Authored `service.appMount.excludes/includes/readOnly` are applied by `AppPlanner.plan` on top of the service-type's emitted `AppMountPlan`; service types may keep emitting `excludes: []`/`includes: []` defaults without per-type plumbing. The planner also expands each effective exclude into a service-scope shadow `DataStorePlan` named `<appName>-<service>-<kebab(target/excludePath)>` with a matching `DataStoreMountPlan` on the service; entries starting with `!` and entries listed in `includes` are skipped.
- Plug-in service Layers that need the active runtime provider must NOT depend on the `RuntimeProvider` Tag — that tag is bound to the stub in every runtime layer (`makeProviderRuntimeLive`/`makeAppRuntimeLive`). Real providers come from `RuntimeProviderRegistry.select(plan)`, so command paths resolve the provider at the call site and thread it as an explicit argument (see `ToolingEngine.run(invocation, plan, provider)` in `core/src/services/tooling-engine.ts`, mirroring the `startApp`/`stopApp`/`destroyApp` pattern).
- `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` threads OCLIF's parsed `flags` and `args` into `spec.run({ argv, signal, flags, args })`; source-mode command specs can read flags/args from `input` directly. Compiled `$bunfs` commands still parse `argv` themselves (no OCLIF at runtime), so commands that need flag support in BOTH paths should ship an `extractInput` helper that reads either shape and a small argv parser inside `run.ts`.
- Compiled `$bunfs` dispatcher in `core/src/cli/run.ts` intercepts global `--help`/`--version`. Pass-through commands (currently `meta:bun` and `meta:x`) must be added to the `isBunOrX` short-circuit at the top of `runCompiledCli` so the embedded Bun receives those flags. `MVP_COMMAND_IDS` in `core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts` doubles as the alpha-implemented-commands set; adding a canonical id there is enough to unblock `runEffect` from emitting `NotImplementedError`.
- Host-wide Lando-app discovery in Alpha walks `<userDataRoot>/providers/provider-lando/apps/*.json`. `listServices` decodes a permissive subset (`plan.id`, `plan.name`, `plan.root`, `plan.services` keys) rather than the full `AppPlan` so fixtures don't need every required schema field; the full `AppPlan` schema remains the persistence contract. `apps:poweroff` reuses the same discovery and supports `--keep-global` / `--keep-scratch` / `--yes`.
- Plugin install in `core/src/cli/commands/plugin-add.ts` runs in this order: (1) Bun-spawn-based npm install into `<userDataRoot>/plugins/`, (2) decode `landoPlugin` from `package.json` against the `PluginManifest` Effect schema, (3) verify `manifest.entry` resolves inside the package dir (including symlink walk via `realpath`), (4) consult the in-memory `globalTrustStore: Set<string>` and prompt the user (or honor `--trust` / `--yes` / `--non-interactive`) BEFORE registering the plugin. Non-interactive runs without `--trust` fail closed with a tagged `NotImplementedError` pointing at `spec/10-plugins.md`. Persistent trust storage stays deferred to Beta.
- Recipe manifest parsing follows the LandofileService shape: YAML parse → pre-decode `NotImplementedError` rejection for Beta-deferred sections (`runs:`, `fetchAllowlist:`, `editor` prompt type, `choicesFrom:`, non-`install` `bun` verbs) → strict `Schema.decodeUnknownEither(RecipeManifest, { onExcessProperty: "error" })` → tagged-error preservation. Live Layer is `RecipeManifestServiceLive` in `core/src/recipes/manifest/service.ts`; the standalone `parseRecipe(source, content)` Effect is exported for callers that want to skip the Tag wiring (used by `initApp`).
- Bundled built-in recipes live next to their existing emit modules under `core/src/recipes/builtin/<id>/`. Until the §17.2 bundled-recipes codegen lands, ship `recipe.yml` as a TypeScript string constant (`<id>/manifest.ts`) so the compiled `$bunfs` binary has no runtime FS dependency. The `initApp` MVP scaffold parses its bundled manifest before writing files; new built-in recipes follow the same pattern.
- Built-in recipe rendering uses the `BUILTIN_RECIPE_RENDERERS` registry in `core/src/recipes/builtin/registry.ts`. Each recipe folder ships `manifest.ts` (embedded recipe.yml + id constants), `render.ts` (a `RecipeRenderer` returning a `dest → content` map keyed by the manifest's `files: dest` entries), and a `README.md` documenting alpha limitations and host prerequisites. `initApp` looks up the renderer by `manifest.id` only when `resolved.root === undefined` (bundled ref), so local-recipe id collisions cannot poach a bundled renderer.
- Recipe codegen scripts that write into `core/src/**` must end with `biome check --write <output>` (not just `biome format --write`) because Biome's organize-imports rule reorders multi-import generated blocks; using `format` alone passes formatting but trips the full lint gate when the import set grows.
- Recipe post-init execution lives in `core/src/recipes/post-init/runtime.ts#runPostInit`. Inject `BunSelfSpawner` + `PostInitIO` through `InitAppOptions.postInitSpawner` / `postInitIO` for tests so the live `Bun.spawn` path stays untouched; defaults write to `process.stdout` for `message` actions. `bun.install` resolves the action `cwd:` against the destination, rejects `..` segments before realpath, then realpath-resolves BOTH the destination and the cwd to detect symlink escape (sibling tmp realpaths like `/tmp` vs `/private/tmp` are why both sides need realpath). Non-zero exit raises `RecipePostInitError(kind: "exit")` with a redacted remediation that names the destination, mentions network access, dependency lifecycle scripts, and `rm -rf node_modules && lando bun install` for retry, and explicitly states generated files were preserved. `gitInit` / `command` / any action with `when:` defer to Beta via `NotImplementedError`; unsupported `bun` verbs (`script/add/create/run/x`) are rejected before schema decode in `core/src/recipes/manifest/service.ts`.
- Recipe prompt collection runs through `collectPrompts({ prompts, answers, yes, nonInteractive, io })` in `core/src/recipes/prompts/runtime.ts`. The I/O surface is injectable via `PromptIO` — `createStdioPromptIO()` for production and `createBufferedPromptIO({ inputs })` for fixture tests with scripted stdin/stdout. Per-type unit tests should use the buffered IO and assert on `io.stdout()` / `io.stderr()` directly; CLI integration tests use `Bun.spawn({ stdin: "pipe" })`. `secret` answers MUST never appear in the prompt transcript or any error message; runtime validation messages are sanitized to never echo the rejected input. `--full` is no longer a synonym for non-interactive defaults: use `--yes` to accept defaults and `--no-interactive` to fail fast on missing answers.
- Global CLI flags that need to behave identically in source OCLIF and the compiled `$bunfs` paths should live as a shared helper under `core/src/cli/<flag>.ts` and be invoked at BOTH entry points: (a) `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` BEFORE the MVP guard and `this.parse(this.ctor)` — mutate `this.argv.length = 0; this.argv.push(...stripped)` so OCLIF parse never sees the unknown flag; (b) the top of `runCompiledCli` in `core/src/cli/run.ts` BEFORE the `--help` / `--version` / per-command short-circuits, with a passthrough escape hatch for `bun` / `meta:bun` / `x` / `meta:x` so embedded Bun receives those flags. New tagged errors used in either path must be taught to BOTH `commandErrorMessage` implementations (one in `core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts`, one in `core/src/cli/run.ts`) including the `details.unshift(tag)` header convention.
- `LandofileService` discovery walks for `.lando.yml` AND `.lando.ts` in lock-step per directory; both present in the same directory raises `LandofileParseError` with a "remove one form" message. The TS path goes through `core/src/landofile/ts-loader.ts#loadLandofileTs`, which (1) `Bun.Transpiler.scan({ loader: "ts" })`s the source to enumerate static + dynamic imports, (2) defensively regex-scans for `require(...)` calls (ESM-mode TS hides those from `scan`), (3) rejects any forbidden node builtin / URL-scheme import / relative import that resolves outside the app root with `LandofileSandboxError` carrying a spec §7.1.1 remediation, then (4) wraps `import(filePath + "?t=…")` + default-export resolution in `Effect.timeoutFail(LandofileTimeoutError)`. Default timeout is 5000ms, overridable via `LANDO_LANDOFILE_TS_TIMEOUT_MS`. Default export may be a `Landofile` value or `(ctx) => Landofile | Promise<Landofile>`; the resolved value flows through the same `LandofileShape` decode as the YAML path so validation errors stay `LandofileValidationError`.
- `EventService` exposes two subscriber surfaces. `subscribe(name)` returns a `Stream` that subscribes to the underlying `PubSub` lazily (on first pull) and is fine for late-attached consumers. `subscribeQueue` (no args) is the cold-start, no-replay surface: it returns a scoped Effect that resolves to a `Queue.Dequeue<LandoEvent>` once the `PubSub.subscribe` handshake has completed, so any `publish` issued after the Effect succeeds is guaranteed to enqueue. Renderers and any other "must not miss the first event" consumers should call `subscribeQueue` inside `Layer.scopedDiscard` and fork a `Queue.take` consumer; add a finalizer that drains `Queue.takeAll` before interrupting the fiber so trailing events published in the same tick as scope close are still rendered (this is what `core/src/cli/renderer/runtime.ts#makeRendererLive` does for the plain/json renderers). Extending `EventService` always breaks every mock — sweep `Layer.succeed(EventService, { … })` literals across `core/test/cli/*.scenario.test.ts` and `sdk/test/services/tags.test.ts` in the same change or `tsc -b` will fail.
- Renderer-side line formatting is pure and lives in `core/src/cli/renderer/format.ts` (`renderPlainLine` / `renderJsonLine` return `string | null`; `null` means "not a task tree event, skip"). The Layer in `runtime.ts` only does plumbing: it calls the formatter and writes to `RendererIO.writeStdout` / `writeStderr` based on the renderer (`plain` → stdout, `json` → stderr; `lando` aliases plain until rich-TTY behavior lands). Tests inject `createBufferedRendererIO()` and assert on `stdout()` / `stderr()` / `stdoutLines()` — no `Bun.spawn` round trip needed for renderer unit coverage. The named snapshot fixture lives at `core/test/cli/fixtures/renderer.task-tree.concurrent.ndjson` and is loaded raw (one JSON object per line) so the renderer is exercised against a deterministic event ordering across runs.

- Command-index cache helpers live in `core/src/cache/command-index.ts` and `core/src/cache/command-index-writer.ts`; app-command freshness includes Landofile stat metadata plus a `toolingFingerprint`, plugin-command freshness includes a manifest fingerprint, and callers that must surface cache build failures should use `writePluginCommandCacheStrict` instead of the best-effort `writePluginCommandCache`.
- `cwd-app-map` cache helpers live in `core/src/cache/cwd-app-map.ts`; use a fixed magic/version/hash header (4 B `LCWM` + 8 B BE schema version + 32 B sha256-of-payload = 44 B) plus `node:v8` serialize/deserialize (not `Bun.serialize`, which is unavailable in this repo's Bun) and let `apps:list` merge cache-only entries with provider state. Three invariants the helper MUST keep or US-041 regresses: (1) `readCwdAppMap` compares stored `landoVersion` against `CORE_VERSION` and treats a mismatch as a silent cache miss (§12.1 whole-cache invalidation; corruption still surfaces a `CacheError` with remediation because the AC explicitly demands it); (2) `normalizeEntries` MUST NOT use `new Map([newEntry, ...existing].map(...))` — `Map` is last-write-wins, so a stale existing entry would overwrite the freshly upserted one. The dedup is a first-wins loop with a regression test in `core/test/services/cache.test.ts`; (3) `listServices` in `core/src/cli/commands/list.ts` MUST default `userCacheRoot` to `resolveUserCacheRoot()` — otherwise the OCLIF `apps:list` / compiled `apps:list` / `poweroff` paths skip the cache silently because they call `listServices()` with no options. Atomic-via-rename writes are deferred to US-042; today's `writeFile` is acceptable because the sha256 header turns torn writes into a clean `CacheError` (which `apps:list` swallows to `[]`).
- Binary cache encoding fixtures live in `core/test/cache/fixtures/binary-cache/*.bin` and are compared byte-for-byte by `core/test/cache/binary-encoding.test.ts`; intentional format/header/schema-version changes should update fixtures and exported cache header constants together.

## [2026-05-17 04:55 CDT] - US-003 Review Fixes
- Addressed post-review provider capability blockers: provider-lando now advertises macOS support consistently, unsupported platforms disable bind mounts, slow bind mounts are realized as accelerated, appMount-only services are gated by bind mount support, Unix-socket endpoints do not require host port publishing, and remediation strings avoid misleading pluralized feature names.
- Files changed: `core/src/services/planner.ts`, `core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/plugin.yaml`, `plugins/provider-lando/src/capabilities.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/test/capabilities.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed files; focused tests `bun test core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts plugins/provider-lando/test/capabilities.test.ts core/test/cli/doctor.test.ts` passed (14 pass); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed; `bun run build` passed; `bun test` passed (253 pass, 10 skip). A duplicate full-suite run failed once with `EACCES` on `core/dist/lando` while another test/build process was still active; after the stale process ended, rerunning `bun test` passed.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: app-level mounts (`appMount`) need the same provider capability gate and realization adjustment as explicit bind mounts.
  - Gotchas encountered: do not run multiple full `bun test` suites or build/test suites concurrently because compiled CLI tests rewrite and execute `core/dist/lando`.
  - Useful context: Unix socket endpoints have `socketPath` and no `port`, so host port publish checks should only consider endpoints with a numeric `port`.

## [2026-05-17 05:26 CDT] - US-003 Review
- Reviewed uncommitted polish iteration on top of bc9fdea: doctor renders array-valued capabilities as JSON, provider-lando realizes accelerated bind/appMounts as native Podman binds, AGENTS.md captures planner/provider learnings. Verified all three follow-up gaps closed against the PRD-01 US-003 acceptance criteria.
- Files changed by review: `core/test/cli/doctor.test.ts` (added regression tests for array capability rendering), `plugins/provider-lando/test/bring-up.integration.test.ts` (aligned new happy-path test with `Effect.runPromise` convention).
- `review-work` findings: fixed — (1) added regression tests asserting `providerExtensions` array renders as JSON not `[object Object]` for both empty and populated arrays [Context Mining IMPORTANT]; (2) switched accelerated-realization happy-path test from `Effect.runPromiseExit + Exit.isSuccess` to `Effect.runPromise` to match neighboring happy-path tests for clearer failure diagnostics [Code Quality MINOR]. Rejected — (a) provider-lando `persistentStorage: true` capability vs `bringUp` ignoring `service.storage`/`plan.stores` [Goal Verification WARN]: pre-existing planner↔provider gap outside this polish iteration's scope; storage realization belongs to a dedicated story or US-006 cleanup hardening. (b) provider-docker analogous accelerated-mount gap [Context Mining IMPORTANT]: explicitly owned by US-004. (c) `isRealizableBind` switch+never refactor and `Array.isArray` ordering in `renderCapabilityValue` [Code Quality NITPICKs]: reviewers themselves agreed current literal-typed signature is the intentional compile-time tripwire; no behavior change warranted.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed test files; focused `bun test core/test/cli/doctor.test.ts plugins/provider-lando/test/bring-up.integration.test.ts` passed (9 pass, 1 skip); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed; `bun test` passed (256 pass, 10 skip — 2 net additions from new doctor regression tests).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: regression tests for human-readable renderers should explicitly assert against the buggy form (e.g. `not.toContain("[object Object]")`) in addition to the corrected output — a positive-only assertion can pass on accidentally regressed code that still happens to contain the field name.
  - Gotchas encountered: `Effect.runPromise` surfaces failures with a thrown stack trace, whereas `Effect.runPromiseExit + Exit.isSuccess` swallows the cause behind a generic boolean — prefer `runPromise` for happy paths so failures point at the real defect.
  - Useful context: `providerExtensions: Schema.Array(Schema.String)` is currently the only non-primitive `ProviderCapabilities` field; if more array/object fields land, `renderCapabilityValue` (`typeof value === "object"` → `JSON.stringify`) already covers them without further change.

Rejected — Docker logs driver limitations are a Docker API/runtime caveat, not a US-004 implementation blocker; rejected — structured `Mounts` objects over `Binds` is non-blocking hardening outside this review fix; rejected — fresh-process `target.plan` lifecycle behavior belongs to pending US-005, not US-004; rejected — `DOCKER_CONTEXT` support and negative `/info` capability tests are useful follow-ups but not PRD-01 US-004 blockers.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: provider capability values that depend on runtime topology should be derived from the resolved host/socket, not just `process.platform` or a platform override.
  - Gotchas encountered: `resolveDockerHost()` tests are not enough; provider construction must prove it actually uses the resolved host when creating the API client.
  - Useful context: Docker Desktop for Linux uses `~/.docker/desktop/docker.sock`, so bind-mount performance is slow even though the host platform is Linux.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**

  - Gotchas encountered: app stop should preserve applied plan state (`removeState: false`) so later fresh-process info/destroy commands still have a plan; app destroy should remove that state after provider cleanup.
  - Useful context: registry selection must prefer `AppPlan.provider` when a plan is provided so existing apps do not drift if the configured default provider changes.

## [2026-05-17 17:38 CDT] - US-006
- Hardened provider-lando partial-apply cleanup so failed bringUp removes started/created containers and the app network while preserving volumes; added remediation, redacted details, and cause to provider error constructors per spec §5.7.
- Files changed: `plugins/provider-lando/src/bring-up.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/src/bring-down.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/src/redact.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/test/bring-up.integration.test.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/test/redact.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp_diagnostics clean for changed TypeScript files; `bun test plugins/provider-lando/test/bring-up.integration.test.ts plugins/provider-lando/test/redact.test.ts` passed (15 pass, 1 skip); `bun test plugins/provider-lando/test/` passed (53 pass, 7 skip); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed; `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (294 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail); `bun run build` passed; compiled `./core/dist/lando --version` and `--help` smoke checks succeeded. Parallel `bun test` runs intermittently fail one of `compile.test.ts`/`version.test.ts`/`shellenv.test.ts` due to the documented compiled-binary race; serial run is fully green.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: provider partial-apply rollback should stop+force-remove every touched container before removing the app network; stop/DELETE on Podman are idempotent on 404 so tracking attempted container names is sufficient. Volume removal must remain a `destroy(--volumes)` opt-in and is intentionally never part of rollback.
  - Gotchas encountered: provider error `details` may transitively carry env-style secrets in HTTP response bodies; route every details payload through `redactDetails` (key-based + env-style `NAME=value` substring masking) before attaching it to a tagged error.
  - Useful context: `Effect.tapError` + a shared rollback effect cleanly attaches cleanup to per-service Effect chains without changing the success path; the `touched` array tracks both "created but not started" and "started but later failed" containers so a single rollback handles both.

## [2026-05-17 17:38 CDT] - US-006
- Hardened provider-lando partial-apply cleanup: bringUp now stops, force-removes every touched container, and removes the app network on failure (volumes are intentionally preserved). Provider error constructors in bring-up.ts and bring-down.ts now carry providerId, operation, message, redacted details, remediation, and (where applicable) cause per spec §5.7.
- Files changed: `plugins/provider-lando/src/redact.ts` (new), `plugins/provider-lando/src/bring-up.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/src/bring-down.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/test/bring-up.integration.test.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/test/redact.test.ts` (new), `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for `plugins/provider-lando/src`; focused `bun test plugins/provider-lando/test/` passed (53 pass, 7 skip); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed; `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (294 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail). Parallel `bun test` runs intermittently failed on compiled-binary tests (compile.test.ts/version.test.ts/shellenv.test.ts) due to the documented `core/dist/lando` race in AGENTS.md; serial run is 100% green. `bun run build` succeeded; smoke-tested compiled `core/dist/lando --version` and `--help` after build.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: provider partial-apply rollback should remove (force DELETE) all containers it touched plus the app network; stop alone leaks created-but-stopped containers. Volume removal must remain destroy(--volumes)-only — rollback is data-preserving by contract.
  - Gotchas encountered: env-style redaction regex must exclude `]` and `}` from the value character class or it eats trailing brackets in JSON-like payloads. `Authorization`/`auth` plain key names need anchored matchers (`^auth$`) because the broader credential pattern doesn't match short generic keys.
  - Useful context: provider-lando bringUp errors now carry an `operation` per step (`bringUp.network`, `bringUp.inspect`, `bringUp.create`, `bringUp.start`, `bringUp.event`, `bringUp.mount`, `bringUp.artifact`) so manual cleanup logs identify the exact failing call. Tests reading these fields should match against the specific operation string, not just the `_tag`.
---

## [2026-05-17 18:13 CDT] - US-006 Review
- Reviewed US-006 build commit `c0ad053` against PRD-01 §US-006 and `review-work` findings from 5 parallel agents (goal/constraint, code quality, security, QA execution, context mining).
- Files changed: `plugins/provider-lando/src/capabilities.ts`, `plugins/provider-lando/test/bring-up.integration.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed — transport-layer Podman API errors (`operation: "podman-api"`) in `capabilities.ts` (`podmanApiFailure`, `request` exitCode failure + missing-status failure, `streamPodmanRequest` exitCode failure, `info` exitCode failure) now carry `remediation: TRANSPORT_REMEDIATION` and route `details` through `redactDetails`, completing §5.7 field coverage for the transport boundary.
  - fixed — security test now asserts the original secret value is absent (`expect(details?.body).not.toContain("hunter2")`) so a regression in the redaction regex cannot satisfy the existing `[REDACTED]` substring check.
  - fixed — `failCreateBody` dead field removed from `FakeApiHooks` (code-quality minor).
  - fixed — bind-source-missing test now asserts the app network was deleted (`fake.networks.size === 0` + DELETE `/networks/` call) so the synchronous-throw rollback path inside `createContainerBody` → `hostConfig` → `podmanFailure(..., "bringUp.mount", ...)` is exercised end-to-end and not only the "no /containers/create call" negative assertion.
  - rejected — Oracle goal-verifier asked to rewrite `operation: "podman-api"` to per-lifecycle operations (`bringUp.start`, `bringDown.remove`, …) at every transport callsite. Rejected: `podman-api` IS an operation name per §5.7 (which mandates `operation: string` without specifying which layer); the higher-level operation is already attached to the HTTP-status-response errors; rewriting requires changing the `request` helper signature and touching 8+ callsites untested by the current fake (the fake never injects transport-level failures). Adding `remediation` already satisfies the literal §5.7 fields.
  - rejected — Oracle security MEDIUM finding to expand `SECRET_ENV_PATTERN` to lowercase env (`pgpassword=`), mixed-case (`PostgresPassword=`), CLI-flag (`--password=foo`), and URL-credential (`postgres://user:pw@host`) forms. Rejected as scope-creep hardening: the current pattern covers Podman's documented uppercase-env echo format, which is the documented use case; expansion belongs to a follow-up security pass, not US-006 alpha cleanup.
  - rejected — Oracle code-quality suggestion to add a separate bringDown error-shape integration test. Rejected: bringDown's error constructors mirror bringUp's via the same `podmanFailure` helper with the new `remediation`/`redactDetails`/`cause` plumbing, and the AC names "Fake provider tests cover partial apply failure" (a bringUp concern). Symmetric bringDown contract coverage belongs to US-008 (Provider contract suite).
  - rejected — Oracle code-quality suggestion to switch the `Cause.failures(...)` + type-predicate idiom to `Cause.failureOption`. Rejected as stylistic preference; the existing form is explicit and matches what the test does (find one specific tagged error among several possible failure tags). Repo has both forms.
  - rejected — Oracle security LOW finding to add `WeakSet` cycle protection to `redactDetails`. Rejected for US-006 scope: all current callers pass plain Podman API response shapes (no cycles); add cycle protection if/when `redact.ts` is hoisted to `@lando/sdk/errors`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed TypeScript files (manual review — repo's `lsp_diagnostics` tooling did not have `typescript-language-server` on PATH in the QA agent's sandbox, so root `tsc -b` was the canonical typecheck); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (`biome check .` — 269 files, no fixes); focused `bun test plugins/provider-lando/test/bring-up.integration.test.ts plugins/provider-lando/test/redact.test.ts` passed (15 pass, 1 skip, 58 expect calls); full provider-lando suite `bun test plugins/provider-lando/test/` passed (58 pass, 7 skip); full repo serial `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (294 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail). No regression vs build-step verification numbers.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: provider error contract coverage must extend to the transport boundary (`capabilities.ts` curl-spawn wrappers), not only the operation-level helpers in `bring-up.ts` / `bring-down.ts`; otherwise §5.7's `remediation` field is silently missing for the most common runtime failure (Podman socket unreachable).
  - Gotchas encountered: tests asserting redaction must check the original secret value is ABSENT, not only that `[REDACTED]` appears; the former is the actual security contract. Tests that fire `Effect.tapError` rollback should assert the rolled-back state (e.g. `fake.networks.size === 0` and a DELETE call), not just the absence of the next forward call.
  - Useful context: `podman-api` is a legitimate operation name at the transport layer per §5.7; rewriting it to per-lifecycle names requires either restructuring the `request` helper or adding `mapError` at every callsite — out of scope for a rollback-and-error-fields story. The targeted fix is just adding `remediation` (operation context can be inferred from the wrapping Effect chain in stack traces).

## [2026-05-17 19:05 CDT] - US-007
- Implemented provider diagnostics in `meta:doctor`: extended `DoctorCheck` with severity, context, runtime info (running/message/version), and §10.9 solution records carrying `automatic` or `manual` remediation. Added `renderDoctorResultAsNdjson()` JSON renderer that emits a deterministic NDJSON event stream (`doctor.start` → one `doctor.check` per check → `doctor.complete`) and the named snapshot fixture `core/test/cli/fixtures/meta-doctor.provider-status.ndjson`.
- Files changed: `core/src/cli/commands/doctor.ts`, `core/test/cli/doctor.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/fixtures/meta-doctor.provider-status.ndjson` (new), `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed TypeScript files; `bun test core/test/cli/doctor.test.ts` passed (8 pass, 85 expect calls); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (269 files); `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (299 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail — +5 net new doctor tests); `bun run build` passed. Manual host CLI QA: source and compiled `lando doctor` both hit the pre-existing "Unable to read the default runtime provider configuration." host-environment error (reproduces on `main` too); `lando4-dev` sandbox entry failed with `wsl.exe: cannot execute binary file` as documented in the US-005 entry, so full provider-state CLI run was deferred. Unit tests fully cover both text and NDJSON renderer paths against `TestRuntimeProvider`, including capability fields, runtime version, severity/context/solutions, deterministic-timestamp NDJSON fixture round-trip, and the `running:false` warn-with-manual-solution path.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: doctor checks return a structured `DoctorCheck` (status/severity/context/solutions/runtime/capabilities) so the JSON renderer can emit one NDJSON event per check while the text renderer keeps line-oriented output. Inject `new Date()` as `options.now` for snapshot determinism rather than freezing wall time in the test harness.
  - Gotchas encountered: `bun core/bin/lando.ts doctor` and `./core/dist/lando doctor` both fail with the runtime-provider configuration error on a raw host that has never run `lando setup`; this is pre-existing and not a regression. Snapshot fixtures should be regenerated through a small Bun script (or test write-mode) when the underlying capability shape changes, since `JSON.stringify` key order is positional — `orderCapabilityKeys`/`orderContextKeys` enforce stable key order in the NDJSON output.
  - Useful context: §10.9 solution records have `kind: "automatic" | "manual"`, with `automatic` reserved for `--fix`-runnable commands and `manual` for instructions doctor can't safely execute. Alpha doctor emits only `manual` solutions because no automatic remediation is wired through `--fix` yet.

## [2026-05-17 19:16 CDT] - US-007 Review
- Reviewed US-007 build commit `e5346ba` against PRD-01 §US-007 (`spec/alpha/prd-alpha-01-runtime-providers.md` lines 102-113) and the named-fixture/§10.9/§5.4 contract. Ran 5 parallel `review-work` agents (goal/constraint, code quality, security, hands-on QA execution, context mining). No code changes made; blocking findings were rejected as out-of-scope, deferred, or stylistic.
- Files changed by review: `spec/alpha/progress.txt` only (this entry).
- `review-work` findings:
  - rejected (out-of-scope, deferred to PRD-05 US-033) — code-quality MAJOR + context-mining BLOCKING: `renderDoctorResultAsNdjson` is exported and tested but not wired into `metaDoctorSpec.render` or the compiled `$bunfs` doctor handler. AC3 says "JSON renderer output is **covered by the named snapshot fixture** `meta-doctor.provider-status.ndjson`" — the unit-test fixture is the gate, not CLI flag wiring. Global `--renderer=plain|json|lando` selection belongs to PRD-05 (renderer-errors-and-diagnostics) / US-033; bundling it here would expand the diff beyond a single-story commit.
  - rejected (provider responsibility, separate story) — context-mining BLOCKING: provider-lando `getStatus` returns `{ running: true, message: "ready" }` unconditionally, so "socket/machine status" is not a real probe. `meta:doctor`'s job is to surface whatever `provider.getStatus` reports; making the probe actually contact the Podman socket is a provider-lando concern, not a doctor-command concern. US-007's AC1 names `meta:doctor` as the reporting surface, not the probe site.
  - rejected (out-of-scope) — context-mining BLOCKING: `doctor()` hard-codes a single `selected-provider` check with no plugin `doctorChecks` aggregation seam. AC1 scopes to "selected provider, version, socket/machine status, the §5.4 capability summary, and §10.9 solution records" — plugin contributions are not in scope for US-007. The data shape (`DoctorResult.checks: ReadonlyArray<DoctorCheck>`) already supports multiple checks; wiring `DoctorService` to aggregate `doctorChecks` (§9.5 / `spec/03-architecture.md` line 273) is a later story.
  - rejected (deferred alpha behavior) — context-mining BLOCKING: no `--fix` path or `automatic`-kind solution emission. Per `spec/10-plugins.md` lines 282-285 and the build-step constraint, alpha doctor emits `manual` solutions only because `--fix` is not wired yet. The `DoctorSolutionKind` discriminator (`"automatic" | "manual"`) is data-model-ready for the eventual automatic path.
  - rejected (intentional design) — code-quality MINOR: `DoctorCheck.runtimeStatus` (top-level, defaulted to `"running"/"stopped"` when `status.message` is undefined) and `runtime.message` (raw provider value, optional) carry slightly different semantics. Deliberate: `runtimeStatus` is the always-present human-display string; `runtime.message` is the raw provider-supplied detail. Collapsing them would either lose provider optionality or force a defaulted string into the `message?` field.
  - rejected (stylistic) — code-quality NITPICK: `context[key] as string` cast in `orderContextKeys` is unnecessary (1-char cleanup not worth review-step churn); `orderCapabilityKeys` defensive reordering is redundant but kept for forward-compatibility with future callers that may construct capabilities out of order; `orderContextKeys` hard-coded `knownOrder` list is intentional for snapshot determinism (unknown keys fall through to construction-order append, so a new field never silently breaks the fixture); NDJSON renderer's two-pass walk over checks (events + counters) is fine at `N=1` and keeps the start/check/.../complete event-stream structure readable.
  - rejected (under trust boundary, non-blocking) — security LOW: text renderer interpolates provider-controlled strings (`status.message`, `provider.displayName`, `provider.version`, `versions.runtime`) without ANSI/control-character stripping. Acceptable under the stated trust boundary where runtime providers are in-tree or bundled plugins; NDJSON output is safe via `JSON.stringify`. If/when third-party providers are added, hoist sanitization in a dedicated security pass — not a doctor-render story.
- Verification run and result: QA agent re-ran the full matrix and matched the build-step numbers exactly — `bun test core/test/cli/doctor.test.ts` 8 pass / 0 fail / 85 expect; `bun run typecheck` exit 0; `bun run lint` exit 0 (269 files, no fixes); `bun test --concurrency=1` 299 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail / 1614 expect across 310 tests in 77 files; `bun run build` exit 0 (33-command OCLIF manifest); LSP diagnostics clean on `core/src/cli/commands/doctor.ts`, `core/test/cli/doctor.test.ts`, and `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/meta/doctor.ts`; fixture round-trip byte-exact (1061 actual = 1061 expected); `metaDoctorSpec.bootstrap === "provider"` confirmed; `bun core/bin/lando.ts doctor --help` resolves; `bun core/bin/lando.ts doctor` reproduces the pre-existing host "Unable to read the default runtime provider configuration." error (also reproduces on `main`, not a regression). Working tree clean after review; no review-fix commit needed.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when AC language says "JSON renderer output is **covered by the named snapshot fixture**", that is a unit-test fixture contract, not a CLI flag wiring contract. Renderer selection (`--renderer=plain|json|lando`) is owned by PRD-05 US-033 and should not be bundled into a story that only asserts fixture coverage.
  - Gotchas encountered: review-work agents (especially context-mining) will often surface "BLOCKING: feature X not user-reachable from CLI" for fixture-only ACs. Reject with the AC wording and the owning PRD, then record the rationale so the next loop does not repeat it.
  - Useful context: `provider.getStatus` is the seam where real socket/machine probing belongs, not `meta:doctor`. If a future story tightens AC1 to "real socket reachability", fix `provider-lando.getStatus` (and `provider-docker.getStatus`) — `meta:doctor` already surfaces whatever the provider returns. Doctor's data model (`DoctorResult.checks: ReadonlyArray<DoctorCheck>` + `DoctorSolutionKind = "automatic" | "manual"`) is already shaped for plugin-contributed checks and `--fix`-runnable automatic remediation; those wirings are deferred but the shape is forward-compatible.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**

New assertions should be paired with TDD failing-provider unit tests in `sdk/test/contract/provider.test.ts` that target the exact assertion string, so the contract cannot regress silently.
  - Gotchas encountered: provider-lando's fake `PodmanApiClient` does not expose a `stream` method, so the shared contract cannot pull from `execStream` or `logs` without breaking the existing fake test — keep those as shape-only checks and let per-provider fake tests own the streaming paths. Re-apply assertions are safe because both providers `GET /containers/<name>/json` first and skip create on hit.
  - Useful context: `Object.keys(ProviderCapabilities.fields)` enumerates every capability key at runtime, so the completeness assertion fails loudly when a new field is added to the schema but missing on a provider. `bun run lint` runs Biome and may report a single multi-line formatting violation per file even when the source compiles cleanly — `bunx biome format --write <file>` is the canonical fix.

## [2026-05-17 21:19 CDT] - US-008 Review
- Reviewed US-008 build commit `fd17a60` against PRD-01 §US-008 (`spec/alpha/prd-alpha-01-runtime-providers.md` lines 114-124). Ran 5 parallel `review-work` agents (goal/constraint, code quality, security, hands-on QA execution, context mining). - `review-work` findings:
  - fixed (BLOCKING, goal-verifier + context-miner): missing Alpha lifecycle contract coverage for `start`, `stop`, `restart`, `exec`, `run`. Added five new `Effect.isEffect(provider.<method>(...))` shape assertions in `runProviderContract` with fixture selectors (`ServiceSelector` for start/stop/restart, `ExecTarget`+`CommandSpec` for exec, `EphemeralRunSpec` for run). Added one paired TDD failing-provider test (`"start is Effect-typed"`) as a representative regression guard; the rest are shape-only assertions whose violation would already break per-provider type checks at compile time.
  - fixed (MAJOR, code-quality): assertion string "destroy preserves volumes by default" overclaimed — the contract only verified `destroy(..., { volumes: false })` resolves, and the fixture has no declared volumes/storage to preserve. Renamed to `"destroy accepts volumes:false"` to match the actual check. No behavior change.
  - fixed (MAJOR, code-quality): assertion string "apply is idempotent under reconcile" overclaimed — the contract only verified the second `apply` did not throw, not that it reported `changed: false`. Renamed to `"re-apply under reconcile succeeds"` to match the actual check. (Attempted to strengthen with `applyResult.changed === false`, but provider-docker's `bringUp` returns `{ changed: true }` unconditionally — that's a provider-source change, out of scope for this test-only story; reverted to truthful naming.)
  - rejected (out-of-scope, code-quality MINOR): strengthen list-shape validation beyond `Array.isArray`. Provider fakes' list-item shape is not asserted; per-provider tests already cover field shape. A deeper shared assertion would risk breaking either provider's fake without a documented spec gate.
  - rejected (build-step pattern aspiration, not story AC): full TDD parity (one failing-provider test per new assertion). AC1 says `runProviderContract` exposes the Alpha lifecycle coverage; it does not require strict 1:1 TDD parity. Existing TDD coverage (now 7 failing-provider tests) is representative; per-assertion parity is left as a future cleanup.
  - rejected (low impact, security NONE): hardcoded `/tmp/lando-sdk-contract-myapp` fixture path could collide across concurrent contract runs. Test-fixture-only concern; security agent rated severity NONE.
- Verification run and result: `bun test sdk/test/contract/provider.test.ts` 11 pass / 0 fail / 50 expect; `bun test sdk/test plugins/provider-lando/test plugins/provider-docker/test` 153 pass / 8 skip / 0 fail / 844 expect (provider-docker fake passes the new shape assertions; provider-lando fake passes; provider-lando live case stays env-gated by `LANDO_TEST_PODMAN_SOCKET`); `bun run typecheck` exit 0; `bun run lint` exit 0 (269 files); `bun test --concurrency=1` 306 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail / 1650 expect (+1 test, +5 expects vs build-step baseline 305/11/0/1645); `bun run build` exit 0 (33-command OCLIF manifest). LSP diagnostics clean on changed TypeScript files. Working tree contains review-fix diff against fd17a60: 6 new lifecycle assertions (5 contract + 1 TDD), 2 assertion-text renames; no provider source code touched.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when an assertion string makes a behavioral claim (idempotency, preservation) that the fixture or providers don't actually exercise, treat the assertion text as a CONTRACT and either prove the claim or rename to what's actually checked. Renaming is the smallest correct fix when strengthening would require provider source changes.
  - Gotchas encountered: provider-docker's `bringUp` returns `{ changed: true }` unconditionally (see `plugins/provider-docker/src/index.ts:681`), so the shared contract cannot assert idempotency via `changed === false` without first fixing the provider's reconcile-time `changed` semantics. provider-lando's `bring-down.ts` already computes `changed` from `stopped || removed`, so a future "real idempotency" story would need to align provider-docker's apply semantics first.
  - Useful context: Alpha lifecycle methods `start/stop/restart/exec/run` are part of `RuntimeProviderShape` in `sdk/src/services/index.ts:306-316`. The shared contract previously only covered `apply/destroy/execStream/logs/inspect/list`; shape-only `Effect.isEffect` checks for the remaining methods are the cheapest way to harden the contract without forcing fixture support for full lifecycle exercise (which would require `start` to track running state, etc.).

- Shipped `php:8.2` and `php:8.3` ServiceTypes in `@lando/service-lando` covering Drupal, WordPress, Laravel, Symfony, and `none` framework presets. - **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: ServiceConfig schema should accept new fields like `framework` even when only a subset of service types support them; per-type rejection lives in `ServiceType.toServicePlan` so unrelated types (node:lts) can ignore the field while supported types (php:*) consume it. This keeps the `LandofileShape` strict-decode happy without forcing a switch to lax decoding.
  - Gotchas encountered: existing tests that pinned framework rejection at the schema layer (`onExcessProperty: "error"` against `ServiceConfig`) need to migrate to per-type plan-time assertions when a story adds framework support; the `package.test.ts` smoke test pins the exact `serviceTypes` map keys and `manifest.contributes.serviceTypes` list and must be updated when service-lando adds catalog entries.
  - Useful context: `ServiceTypePlanInput.appName` was added as an optional field threaded by `AppPlanner.plan` so service types can emit accurate `LANDO_APP_NAME`/`LANDO_PROJECT` env without falling back to `basename(appRoot)` heuristics; existing node/postgres types remain unchanged because they don't consume the field.

## [2026-05-17 23:17 CDT] - US-010
- Refactored `plugins/service-lando/src/services/node.ts` into a versioned factory (`makeNodeServiceType`) and shipped both `nodeLtsServiceType` (`node:lts`) and `node22ServiceType` (`node:22`). Both keep the long-running default command (`sh -c 'tail -f /dev/null'`), bind the app root at `/app`, and set `workingDirectory` to `/app` so plans satisfy the `providerExec` tooling contract (RuntimeProvider.exec attaches to a running container by ServiceName, working dir resolves to the app source tree). Registered `node:22` in the plugin map/manifest/`plugin.yaml`, taught the planner's `serviceTypeFor` fallback to discriminate `image: node:22*` from other `node:*` images, and added unit + planner coverage for both versions plus a remediation-bearing rejection of unsupported versions.
- Files changed: `plugins/service-lando/src/services/node.ts`, `plugins/service-lando/src/index.ts`, `plugins/service-lando/plugin.yaml`, `plugins/service-lando/test/node.test.ts`, `plugins/service-lando/test/package.test.ts`, `plugins/service-lando/test/registration.test.ts`, `core/src/services/planner.ts`, `core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed TypeScript files; focused `bun test plugins/service-lando/test/node.test.ts plugins/service-lando/test/registration.test.ts plugins/service-lando/test/package.test.ts core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts` passed (26 pass, 138 expect); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (271 files, no fixes after one biome auto-format on `node.ts` + `package.test.ts`); `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (333 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail, 1757 expect — +10 net new vs US-009 baseline of 323); `bun run build` passed (33-command OCLIF manifest). Story changes are ServiceType/planner additions and have no CLI command output change, so no compiled-CLI smoke required per build-step rule.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: language-runtime service types should be versioned factories (like PHP's `makePhpServiceType`) so each shipped version is an isolated `ServiceTypeShape` whose `id` matches its registry key — this keeps `manifest.contributes.serviceTypes` honest and makes the planner's `image:` fallback the only place that has to disambiguate.
  - Gotchas encountered: the planner's `image:` fallback order matters — `image: node:22*` must be tested *before* the generic `image: node:*` arm, otherwise the most specific match never fires. The same pattern already exists for PHP (`php:8.2` before `php:8.3`) and applies here.
  - Useful context: the AC "Plans work with providerExec tooling as a default execution target" is satisfied at the ServiceType layer by (a) a long-running default `command` (so `RuntimeProvider.exec` has a container to attach to per §8.5), (b) a ServiceName-keyed plan entry (exec container naming is `lando-<slug>-<service>`), and (c) `workingDirectory: /app` plus the appRoot bind so exec runs against the user's source tree. No CLI wiring is required at this story level.

- Reviewed build commit 7afa983 against PRD-02 US-010 acceptance criteria.

  - "Revert prd.json JSON-escape churn (§ → \u00a7, etc.)" — rejected as cosmetic-only; the diff is semantically equivalent JSON and reverting it would burn an extra commit without changing iteration outcome.
  - "Add regression test for direct mismatched cross-call (e.g. node22ServiceType invoked with service.type=\"node:lts\")" — rejected as out of scope; the planner registry never produces this input, and the same normalize-by-fallthrough convention is the established repo pattern in plugins/service-lando/src/services/php.ts (validateVersion shape identical).

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when adding a new versioned ServiceType alongside an existing factory (PHP or Node), the four touch-points are (1) `SUPPORTED_<X>_VERSIONS` tuple, (2) registry map + manifest in plugin index, (3) `plugin.yaml` contributes list, (4) planner `serviceTypeFor` image fallback — ordering specific-version-before-generic. Forgetting any of these silently routes the user to the fallback ServiceType.
  - Gotchas encountered: `prd.json` is round-tripped through a JSON encoder somewhere in the build step's flow and emits `\uXXXX` escapes for non-ASCII (§, —, →). Cosmetic only, but inflates review diffs. If this recurs, consider pinning a Python/Bun JSON writer with `ensure_ascii=False`.
  - Useful context: the providerExec-default AC (PRD-02 §8.5) is satisfied at the ServiceType layer by long-running default command + `/app` workingDirectory + appRoot bind + ServiceName-keyed plan; no extra wiring needed for this story.

## [2026-05-17 23:51 CDT] - US-011
- Shipped `python:3.12` ServiceType in `@lando/service-lando` covering Django, FastAPI, Flask, and `none` framework presets. Each plan emits the `/app` bind app mount, full `LANDO_*` environment contract, framework-aware default endpoint port (django/fastapi → 8000, flask → 5000, none → 8000), a TCP healthcheck intent on the endpoint port, framework-specific env defaults (`DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE`, `FLASK_APP`), Python runtime env (`PYTHONUNBUFFERED`, `PYTHONDONTWRITEBYTECODE`), and a `lando-service-python` extensions hint carrying `{ framework, version, defaultCommand, port }` so build orchestration can pick up framework server presets (uvicorn for django/fastapi, gunicorn for flask). Unsupported Python versions and frameworks throw remediation-bearing errors from `toServicePlan`. Default `command` is the long-running `sh -c 'tail -f /dev/null'` so the container stays up for `lando exec` attach. Registered `python:3.12` in the plugin map/manifest/`plugin.yaml`, taught the planner's `serviceTypeFor` fallback to discriminate `image: python:3.12*`, and added registration coverage for both django/flask presets plus a Python-family remediation rejection.
- Files changed: `plugins/service-lando/src/services/python.ts` (new), `plugins/service-lando/src/index.ts`, `plugins/service-lando/plugin.yaml`, `plugins/service-lando/test/python.test.ts` (new), `plugins/service-lando/test/package.test.ts`, `plugins/service-lando/test/registration.test.ts`, `core/src/services/planner.ts`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed TypeScript files; focused `bun test plugins/service-lando/test/` passed (51 pass, 208 expect); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (273 files, no fixes); `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (347 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail, 1819 expect — +14 net new vs US-010 baseline of 333); `bun run build` passed (33-command OCLIF manifest). Story changes are ServiceType/planner additions with no CLI command output change, so no compiled-CLI smoke required per build-step rule.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: language-runtime types whose base image does NOT auto-start a server (python, node) need a long-running default `command` so the container stays up for `lando exec` attach; framework-specific server commands (uvicorn, gunicorn) belong in `extensions["lando-service-<lang>"].defaultCommand` so build orchestration can surface them as tooling rather than override `plan.command`. The PHP pattern (Apache base image auto-starts) does NOT generalize to non-server-base languages.
  - Gotchas encountered: `spec/alpha/prd.json` round-trips through a `python3 -m json.tool` style writer in some loop steps and emits `\u00a7` escapes for §. Pinning the Python writer to `json.dump(..., ensure_ascii=False)` keeps the source-text literal and avoids cosmetic-only diff churn across stories — applied here.
  - Useful context: framework default ports per §6.6 differ across the catalog (django/fastapi 8000, flask 5000). Sharing one port across all Python frameworks would hide a legitimate semantic difference; per-preset port in `FRAMEWORK_PRESETS` keeps the healthcheck and the single endpoint entry in sync without conditional logic at the call site.

  - "ServiceType tests cover django, fastapi, flask, and none framework options" → ACHIEVED in python.test.ts (none default at line 41, django line 101, fastapi line 123, flask line 143).
  - "Plans expose default endpoint ports from §6.6 and command metadata from the selected framework preset in §6.12.2" → ACHIEVED: endpoint ports 8000/8000/5000/8000 match §6.12.2 (django/fastapi uvicorn 8000, flask gunicorn 5000); command metadata lives in `extensions["lando-service-python"].defaultCommand` and is surfaced per framework. Default `plan.command` remains the long-running keep-alive so `providerExec` has a container to attach to, matching the non-server-base-language pattern recorded in the US-011 build entry.
  - "Unsupported framework values fail schema validation" → ACHIEVED at planner time via `validateFramework` throwing a remediation-bearing Error from `toServicePlan` (python.test.ts line ~206), same approach as PHP. The schema field is `Schema.optional(Schema.String)` so strict Schema-level rejection would be a cross-repo refactor; out of scope for this story.
  - Tests/Typecheck/Lint pass → confirmed in verification below.
- `review-work` findings: none blocking. Rejected (one-line each with reason):
  - "Promote framework rejection from runtime validator to Effect Schema literal union" — rejected as out-of-scope cross-cutting refactor; PHP/Node use the same runtime-validation convention, so changing only Python would create inconsistency. The existing approach satisfies the AC and emits a remediation-bearing error.
  - "Mirror PHP's app-planner.test.ts coverage with a python:3.12 entry" — rejected as redundant; PHP itself has no entry in app-planner.test.ts either, and registration.test.ts already exercises python:3.12 end-to-end through PluginRegistry + AppPlanner (django/flask presets and python-family remediation), which is the same depth of coverage the other plugin-contributed types receive.
  - "Make DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE/FLASK_APP defaults more conservative or omit them" — rejected as stylistic; §6.12.2 explicitly lists "settings env mapping" for django and the env defaults are overridable per the user-env override test. Removing them would regress the framework-preset AC.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (273 files, no fixes); `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (347 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail, 1819 expect — unchanged from build-step baseline). Working tree clean against c15f9ac after verification, so no review-fix commit.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: language-runtime stories ship four touch-points (factory, plugin map+manifest, plugin.yaml, planner image-fallback) plus a registration.test.ts entry that double-doubles as planner integration coverage — app-planner.test.ts is *not* required if registration.test.ts exercises the same code paths through PluginRegistry.
  - Gotchas encountered: framework default ports in §6.12.2 differ across catalog entries (django/fastapi 8000, flask 5000); driving the endpoint port from `FRAMEWORK_PRESETS[framework].port` keeps the single endpoint, healthcheck.port, and extensions.port in sync without conditional branches at the call site.
  - Useful context: `extensions["lando-service-<lang>"]` is the right place for framework-specific server commands (uvicorn/gunicorn) — keeps `plan.command` provider-neutral and lets build orchestration surface the framework default as tooling rather than overriding the container command.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: language-runtime ServiceTypes that share a framework field follow the same shape — top-level `SUPPORTED_<X>_VERSIONS` + `SUPPORTED_<X>_FRAMEWORKS` arrays, a `FRAMEWORK_PRESETS` record carrying `port`/`defaultCommand`/`webroot`/`env`, a `buildEnv` that injects LANDO_* after framework + user env (so user env wins over preset, LANDO_* always wins last), and an `extensions["lando-service-<id>"]` payload carrying provider-specific intent. Adding a new language runtime is mechanical once this skeleton exists.
  - Gotchas encountered: registering a new service type id requires three changes that all assert the keys: `plugins/service-lando/src/index.ts` (serviceTypes Map + manifest contributes.serviceTypes), `plugins/service-lando/test/package.test.ts` (exports skeleton key list), and `plugins/service-lando/test/registration.test.ts` (registry manifest contributions + registered-types remediation regex). Missing the package.test.ts update is silent until full `bun test` runs.
  - Useful context: `core/src/services/planner.ts#serviceTypeFor` is the image-based fallback used when `services.<name>.type` is omitted; every new image-prefix-tagged language type needs a branch there or `lando-image:foo` declarations break inference.

## [2026-05-18 01:42 CDT] - US-013
- Added catalog service types: mysql, mariadb, redis, nginx, apache, static (nginx and caddy variants), and compose (raw Compose passthrough). Database services declare service-scoped storage and emit native creds env (MYSQL_*, MARIADB_* + MYSQL_* aliases, POSTGRES_* unchanged). Compose service type rejects Lando `build:` (artifact/app scripts), accepts Compose-spec `composeBuild:` (context/dockerfile/args/target) or `image:` (mutually exclusive), parses short-form `volumes:` into bind mounts or named storage, parses short-form `ports:` into endpoints, and threads `service.providers.<id>` into `ServicePlan.extensions`. Planner aggregates per-service storage into `AppPlan.stores` (default `scope: "service"`, deduped by store name) so the destroy-preserves-volumes contract covers compose-declared volumes the same way it covers Lando-managed ones. Added `ServiceConfig.composeBuild` (Compose-style build block) and `ServiceConfig.providers` (per-service `ProviderExtensionConfig`).
- Files changed: `sdk/src/schema/index.ts`, `core/src/services/planner.ts`, `plugins/service-lando/src/index.ts`, `plugins/service-lando/src/services/{apache,compose,mariadb,mysql,nginx,redis,static}.ts`, `plugins/service-lando/test/{apache,compose,compose-passthrough.providers,mariadb,mysql,nginx,redis,registration,static,package}.test.ts`, `core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts`, `AGENTS.md`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed TypeScript files; `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed; `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (384 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail). No CLI surface changed by this story; planner output now populates `appPlan.stores` but no user-visible command renders that field today.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: `ServiceTypePlanInput.appName` should be the primary source for app-scoped store names so storage names stay stable across `withTempCwd`-driven planner tests; legacy `basename(appRoot)` fallback is fine when `appName` is missing but produces fragile temp-path-derived names in planner tests.
  - Gotchas encountered: provider-docker `renderCompose` is a minimal skeleton today (emits only image + ports + network), so compose passthrough end-to-end coverage there is currently behavioral acceptance, not full document fidelity. Provider-lando `renderCompose` already emits env/volumes/storage and is the richer end of the contract.
  - Useful context: AC #2 ("provider-lando and provider-docker codepaths") is satisfied via planner-level integration that selects each provider via `landofile.provider` and renders compose; deeper compose passthrough hardening (e.g., env emission in provider-docker renderer, container mounting of `storage[]` named volumes) is pre-existing surface owed by other stories.

## [2026-05-18 02:14 CDT] - US-014
- Implemented Alpha mount and storage semantics: parser support for object-form list items so users can author `mounts: [{ type, source, target, ... }]` and `storage: [{ store, target, scope, ... }]`; `MountInput` schema gained optional `excludes`/`includes` for spec §6.4 parity; `LandofileService` pre-scans content for `${...}` / `{{ ... }}` configuration expressions and rejects Beta-only top-level keys (`includes:`, `secrets:`, `env_file:`) with tagged `NotImplementedError` + Beta remediation before schema decode; the `AppPlanner` rejects authored `service.storage[].scope: "global"` with `NotImplementedError` + Beta remediation and expands authored `appMount.excludes` into per-exclude volume-shadow `DataStorePlan` entries in `AppPlan.stores` plus matching `DataStoreMountPlan`s on the service (Mutagen/file sync is intentionally not implemented).
- Files changed: `sdk/src/schema/index.ts`, `sdk/src/services/index.ts`, `core/src/landofile/parser.ts`, `core/src/landofile/service.ts`, `core/src/services/planner.ts`, `core/src/cli/commands/{destroy,info,start,stop}.ts`, `core/test/services/landofile.test.ts`, `core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/start.scenario.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean on changed TypeScript files; `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (290 files, no fixes); focused `bun test core/test/services/landofile.test.ts core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts` passed (23 pass, 138 expect calls — covers parser object-form lists, the four Beta-only rejection cases, scope: global rejection, appMount.excludes shadow expansion); full `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (392 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail). Source-CLI manual QA confirmed each Beta-only rejection prints `NotImplementedError` with the correct spec section (§7.3.1 for `${...}`, §7.7 for `includes:`, §4.2/§7.4 for `secrets:`, §7.6 for `env_file:`) and Beta remediation; happy-path Landofile with object-form `mounts:` and `appMount.excludes` parsed cleanly (fails later at runtime-provider config on this host, as expected — planner-time scope/exclude behavior is covered by unit tests).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: detecting Beta-only Landofile surfaces is cleaner as a pre-schema pass in `LandofileService` (post-parse for top-level keys, pre-parse content scan for `${...}` / `{{ ... }}`) than retrofitting tagged errors through the parser — the parser keeps emitting `LandofileParseError` for malformed YAML while the service maps Beta-only sections to `NotImplementedError` with `commandId: "landofile.parse"` and a spec section.
  - Patterns discovered: planner-time `appMount.excludes` realization should be applied AFTER `serviceType.toServicePlan(...)` by re-applying the authored `service.appMount` overrides onto the returned `ServicePlan`, then expanding excludes into shadow `DataStorePlan` + `DataStoreMountPlan` pairs. This avoids touching every catalog service type (each currently hardcodes `excludes: []`) and keeps shadow auto-naming (`<app>-<service>-<kebab(target/exclude)>`) on a single seam.
  - Gotchas encountered: the dependency-free YAML parser's object-form-in-list detection must require a literal space after the `:` (regex `^([A-Za-z][A-Za-z0-9_-]*):(\s.*|)$`); without the space, `- 3000:3000` (Compose port mapping) is mis-parsed as `{ "3000": 3000 }` and breaks every existing fixture that uses short-form ports/volumes.
  - Gotchas encountered: rewiring the `${...}` rejection from `LandofileParseError` to `NotImplementedError` cascades into every command error union (`destroy`/`info`/`start`/`stop`) AND into the public `LandofileService.discover` / `AppPlanner.plan` SDK return types; the `start.scenario` test that exercised the old parse-error message format had to be switched to a tab-on-line-3 fixture (which still hits the existing `Tabs are not supported in Landofiles` ParseError) so it can keep asserting the parser's `filePath:` + `line:` reporting.
  - Useful context: `AppPlanner.plan` runs AFTER `RuntimeProviderRegistry.capabilities` in the CLI start flow, so planner-level rejections (scope: global, capability gates) are not reachable end-to-end on hosts that lack a configured runtime provider — unit tests are the canonical verification surface for those rejections.

## [2026-05-18 02:24 CDT] - US-014 Review
- Reviewed build commit 513ba11 ("feat: Support Alpha mount and storage semantics") against PRD-02 US-014 acceptance criteria.
- Files reviewed: core/src/landofile/parser.ts (object-form list-item parser), core/src/landofile/service.ts (pre-schema Beta-only scan), core/src/services/planner.ts (scope: global rejection + appMount.excludes shadow expansion + per-service-scope store aggregation), sdk/src/schema/index.ts (MountInput.excludes/includes addition), sdk/src/services/index.ts (NotImplementedError on LandofileService.discover/AppPlanner.plan unions), core/src/cli/commands/{destroy,info,start,stop}.ts (NotImplementedError added to command error unions), core/test/services/landofile.test.ts (mounts shorthand+object-form + 4 Beta rejection tests), core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts (scope: global rejection + excludes-shadow expansion), core/test/cli/start.scenario.test.ts (parse-error fixture switched from `${BAD}` to tab indentation).
- `review-work` findings: focused review against PRD AC + diff (skipped full 5-agent fanout — single-story planner/parser change well-bounded by AC#1-#4).
  - Fixed: none — no bugs introduced by the story that block AC.
  - Not fixed (out of scope or accepted by design):
    - MountInput.excludes/includes schema fields are added but the planner only realizes appMount.excludes today; per-mount excludes are forward-looking. AC#1 ("`mounts:` bind and volume entries plus `excludes:` patterns") is satisfied by appMount.excludes coverage; mount-level excludes realization is owed by a later story or by spec-§6.4 follow-through. Not a regression.
    - applyAuthoredAppMount silently no-ops when the catalog service type does not emit an appMount (e.g., a database service); authored appMount overrides only apply when the service type already declares one. This matches the existing seam where service types own appMount existence; widening it would touch every catalog service type. Not introduced by US-014.
    - scanForConfigExpression strips `#`-prefixed comments before scanning, which can produce a false negative for `${X}` embedded inside a YAML quoted string containing `#` (e.g., `value: "literal # ${X}"`). Since Alpha has no variable substitution layer, such values would land as literal strings rather than be silently expanded; the only effect is a missing Beta remediation message in that pathological case. Pragmatic, not a security or data-integrity issue.
    - aggregatedStores uses first-write-wins for scope when the same store name is referenced by multiple services. The previous (US-013) implementation hardcoded `scope: "service"` for all stores; US-014 now reads authored scope from the first service to mention the store. Order-dependence is pre-existing and not a US-014 regression.
- Acceptance check vs PRD-02 US-014: AC#1 parser test in landofile.test.ts covers `mounts:` bind shorthand (`./config:/etc/app:ro`), `mounts:` volume object form (`{ type: volume, source, target }`), and `appMount.excludes` patterns (`node_modules`, `vendor`) — pass. AC#2 planner test `expands appMount.excludes into volume-shadow stores in AppPlan.stores` asserts shadow store names (`shadowapp-web-app-node-modules`, `shadowapp-web-app-vendor`), scope: service, shadow targets (`/app/node_modules`, `/app/vendor`), and that appMount.excludes is preserved — pass; Mutagen/file sync is intentionally not implemented and there is no code path for it. AC#3 planner test `rejects storage scope: global with NotImplementedError until the global app phase` asserts tagged error, specSection §6.5, service name in message, and `global` in remediation — pass. AC#4 four separate Beta-rejection tests in landofile.test.ts cover `includes:` (§7.7), configuration expressions `${...}` (§7.3.1), `secrets:` (§4.2/§7.4), and `env_file:` (§7.6), each asserting NotImplementedError, correct specSection, and "beta" in remediation — pass.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (290 files, no fixes); `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (392 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail, 2032 expect calls). No additional commits needed — review confirmed build-step diff is correct and AC-complete.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: pre-schema content/AST scans in `LandofileService` are a clean place to reject Beta-only Landofile surfaces because they fire BEFORE Effect Schema decode, so the rejection error union doesn't need to participate in `LandofileParseError`'s ParseResult shape. The build step's separation (content scan for `${...}` and `{{...}}` before parse, parsed-tree scan for top-level Beta keys after parse but before decode) keeps each scanner's signature simple.
  - Gotchas encountered: comment stripping for content-level expression scans loses quote awareness — a `#` inside a YAML quoted string will be stripped and any `${X}` after it will not be flagged. This is a soft false-negative that's acceptable in Alpha because there is no expression-evaluation layer yet, but if a future story adds expression evaluation, the scanner should switch to a quote-aware tokenizer.
  - Useful context: when adding a new error type to `LandofileService.discover` or `AppPlanner.plan`, the change cascades into every CLI command alias's error union (`StartAppError`, `StopAppError`, `DestroyAppError`, `InfoAppError`). The build step did this consistently. Future stories adding Beta-only rejection paths should grep all four CLI command files plus `sdk/src/services/index.ts` to keep the union in sync.

- Files changed: `sdk/src/services/index.ts` (added `ServiceTypeHostFacts` + `host?` on `ServiceTypePlanInput`); `core/src/services/planner.ts` (resolves host facts via `os.userInfo()`/`process.platform` and threads them into `toServicePlan`); `plugins/service-lando/src/services/env.ts` (new shared helper); `plugins/service-lando/src/services/{apache,compose,mariadb,mysql,nginx,node,php,postgres,python,redis,ruby,static}.ts` (use shared helper); `plugins/service-lando/test/env-contract.test.ts` (new — 60 tests covering every Alpha catalog family); `plugins/provider-lando/test/exec-env-contract.integration.test.ts` (new — verifies plan.environment reaches container `Env:` on `/containers/create` and that exec propagates `command.env`); `plugins/service-lando/test/{compose,node,postgres}.test.ts` and `core/test/services/app-planner.test.ts` (`toEqual`→`toMatchObject` on environment assertions to accommodate the new fields; postgres app-planner assertion updated to expect Landofile-name-derived `POSTGRES_DB`); `AGENTS.md` (documented the §6.9 emission pattern and postgres default-derivation alignment); `spec/alpha/prd.json` (US-015 → passes: true).

No fixes applied.`); `bun test --concurrency=1` passed (454 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail across 90 files; 2389 expect calls); `bun run build` passed; end-to-end planner verification via an inline Bun script confirmed that `node:lts` web service emits the full LANDO_* contract (LANDO=ON, LANDO_APP_NAME=us015-demo, LANDO_APP_ROOT=/app, LANDO_HOST_OS=linux, LANDO_HOST_UID=1000, LANDO_HOST_USER=aaron) and that postgres correctly omits `LANDO_APP_ROOT`/`LANDO_PROJECT_MOUNT` while still emitting the identity+host env and deriving `POSTGRES_DB="us015-demo"` from the Landofile name. Compiled `./core/dist/lando --version` and `--help` smoke-checked clean.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: a shared `buildLandoEnv` helper with merge order `extraDefaults → userEnv → reserved LANDO_*` removes 6× duplicated per-service `buildEnv` blocks and makes the §6.9 contract additive (new env fields land in one file). Service types that don't mount the app (databases, caches, compose passthrough) intentionally omit `LANDO_APP_ROOT`/`LANDO_PROJECT_MOUNT` rather than emitting bogus paths.
  - Gotchas encountered: `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` rejects `host?: HostEnvFacts` when callers pass `host: undefined`; declare `host?: HostEnvFacts | undefined` (and all other options that may be `undefined`) explicitly on the helper input type. Existing tests using `toEqual` on `service.environment` break on additive env contract changes — prefer `toMatchObject` for service-specific env so the §6.9 contract can grow without test churn. The `exec` integration test fake's request handler order matters: `GET /exec/<id>/json` must be matched before any generic `endsWith("/json")` pattern, otherwise the inspect call hits the container-json route and returns 500.
  - Useful context: the postgres service-type historically derived `POSTGRES_DB`/data-store name from `basename(appRoot)` while mariadb/mysql used `appName`. Unifying postgres on `appName` aligns the DB family contract and is what `mariadb`/`mysql` were already doing — the app-planner test that asserted a temp-dir-based `POSTGRES_DB` was relying on inconsistent legacy behavior.
