## [2026-05-19 09:25 CDT] - US-014b Review
- Reviewed the US-014b build commit (HEAD `8500f91 feat: Extend LandofileService to load \`landofile.ts\``) against PRD-02 US-014b acceptance criteria and spec §7.1.1. Ran `Skill(review-work)` fan-out (5 parallel agents: goal/constraint, code-quality, security, QA hands-on, context-mining). Three convergent in-scope bugs surfaced and were fixed with the smallest correct change; the broader sandbox-completeness findings (same-process eval, `Bun.*` globals, top-level side effects) were rejected as out-of-scope for a single-story review fix and recorded as a documented Alpha trust-boundary instead.
- Files changed by review: `core/src/landofile/service.ts` (pipe TS output through `rejectBetaTopLevelKeys`/`rejectBetaToolingFeatures`), `core/src/landofile/ts-loader.ts` (broaden `FORBIDDEN_REQUIRE_REGEX` to cover `(require)("x")` + back-tick template literals; reset `lastIndex` defensively; route `Effect`/`Promise`/value default-exports through a shared `resolveLandofileResult` that runs Effects via `Effect.runPromise`), `core/test/services/landofile-ts.test.ts` (five new tests: TS `{ includes }` → NotImplementedError §7.7, TS Beta tooling field → NotImplementedError, template-literal `require(\`node:fs\`)` → LandofileSandboxError, parenthesized `(require)("node:fs")` → LandofileSandboxError, function-form `Effect.succeed(...)` resolves), `AGENTS.md` (expanded gotcha to record the broadened require()-regex shape, the Effect-return default-export path, the new TS-form Beta-rejection wiring, and an explicit Alpha trust-boundary note).
- `review-work` findings:
  - fixed [P1 QA / MAJOR code-quality / IMPORTANT context-mining] "TS Landofile returning `{ includes: [...] }` surfaces a generic `LandofileValidationError`, but the equivalent YAML emits `NotImplementedError(§7.7)` with the Beta remediation": piped `loadTsLandofile` through `rejectBetaTopLevelKeys` and `rejectBetaToolingFeatures` after the loader returns. Two parametrized tests now assert TS-form `{ includes }` and TS-form tooling `{ deps }` produce the same tagged error the YAML path emits — closing the AC4 "same error shape as YAML path" gap that the build step had unintentionally left open.
  - fixed [P1 QA / MEDIUM security / NITPICK code-quality] "`require(\`node:fs\`)` and `(require)("node:fs")` escape the static-scan sandbox": rewrote `FORBIDDEN_REQUIRE_REGEX` to `(?:\brequire\b|\(\s*require\s*\))\s*\(\s*(?:"([^"]*)"|'([^']*)'|\`([^\`$]*)\`)\s*\)/g` so all three opening forms × all three quote types are caught; updated `scanRequireCalls` to read whichever capture group fired and to reset `lastIndex` on entry. Two new tests lock in the template-literal and parenthesized-`(require)` rejections.
  - fixed [IMPORTANT context-mining / PARTIAL goal-verifier] "Function-form `.lando.ts` default-export does not detect `Effect.Effect<Landofile, LandofileError>` return values, despite spec §7.1.1 listing that shape": refactored `unwrapDefault` to route any non-null object through a new `resolveLandofileResult` that checks `Effect.isEffect`, runs via `Effect.runPromise` inside the existing `Effect.timeoutFail` envelope, recurses on thenables, and otherwise returns the value. New test exercises a function-form `() => Effect.succeed({...})` and asserts the resolved Landofile.
  - rejected [HIGH security / BLOCKING goal-verifier / MAJOR code-quality] "Same-process `import(...)` allows arbitrary `Bun.spawn`/`Bun.write`/`fetch`/`eval`/`new Function` execution and `process.env` read access; this is not actually a sandbox": correct observation, but a real sandbox requires worker/subprocess isolation with a capability-injected IO surface — that is a story-sized re-architecture, not a single-commit review fix. AGENTS.md now carries an explicit Alpha trust-boundary note ("treat `.lando.ts` as trusted author-code"); the spec-mandated `LandofileTopLevelSideEffectError` and worker-evaluation work are deferred to a follow-up story.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "`LandofileFormConflictError` is mandated by spec §7.1.1 but the implementation uses `LandofileParseError`": cosmetic at runtime — both classes carry the same `message` field and surface through the same CLI printer with the same remediation, and adding a new tagged error class would transitively widen every CLI command error alias again. Defer to a follow-up that lands the error catalog cleanup alongside the worker-isolation story.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining / PARTIAL goal-verifier] "Full `LandofileContext` (`layer`, `mergeAccumulator`, `secrets`) is missing from the function-form ctx; spec §7.1.1 lists all three": these fields depend on the §7.2 layered-merge work and the §4.2 `SecretStore` deferred-resolver, neither of which has landed. Wiring them now would either be a no-op stub (`layer: "canonical"`, `mergeAccumulator: undefined`, `secrets.read = () => Effect.die(...)`) that future agents would have to special-case, or it would require landing §7.2 layered merge in the same commit. Defer to the layered-merge story.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "Layered TS forms (`.lando.base.ts`, `.lando.dist.ts`, `.lando.upstream.ts`, `.lando.local.ts`, `.lando.user.ts`) are not discovered/merged": again tied to the §7.2 layered-merge story. The current discovery walks `.lando.yml`/`.lando.ts` at the canonical layer only, which matches the existing YAML behavior — adding layered TS now would require implementing the YAML layered counterpart in the same change.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "Timeout config diverges from spec `landofile.tsTimeoutMs:` global config; implementation uses `LANDO_LANDOFILE_TS_TIMEOUT_MS` env var only": Alpha-acceptable divergence already documented in the build step's progress entry and in AGENTS.md; the global-config surface for `landofile.tsTimeoutMs:` is unimplemented at the §7 global-config layer too. Defer alongside the global-config story.
  - rejected [IMPORTANT context-mining] "US-029 (recipe emits `.lando.ts`) is not exercised by tests": US-029 is its own story (PRD-04). US-014b's AC scope is "loader exists and YAML/TS forms produce equivalent Landofile values" — the YAML/TS equivalence test in `core/test/services/landofile-ts.test.ts` covers that. Recipe-emits-`.lando.ts` coverage belongs to US-029.
  - rejected [MEDIUM security / MAJOR code-quality] "Symlink-based relative-import escape: `appRoot/inner.ts` could be a symlink pointing to `/etc/passwd`": realpath-based containment requires async `fs.realpath` inside the static-scan path and a corresponding error tag for the "scan target moved during scan" race. Defer to the worker-isolation story alongside the same-process-eval rescope.
  - rejected [LOW security] "`?t=Date.now()` cache-buster collisions and memory leak in long-running embedding hosts": affects library-mode embedding only (PRD-06 §16); CLI is short-lived. Defer to the library-mode cache story alongside the §12.1 `app-plan` cache work.
  - rejected [NITPICK code-quality] "`host.os` and `host.platform` are identical `NodeJS.Platform` values": spec lists distinct fields but the runtime distinction depends on the §7.3.1 expression-scope work; for now they're aliases. Defer to the §7.3.1 host-context story.
  - rejected [NITPICK code-quality] "`withTempCwd`/`withEnv` mutate process-global state and would flake under concurrent test execution": Bun runs tests serially within a file by default; the timeout test's 120ms threshold is conservative because the assertion only checks that the failure tag is `LandofileTimeoutError`, not exact elapsed time. Acceptable for Alpha.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed (clean `tsc -b`); `bun run lint` passed (`biome check .` 389 files, no fixes — required a single-quote/double-quote swap on one new test name after the formatter flagged it); `bun test` passed (772 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail, 3599 expect() — +5 tests / +62 expect() vs. the build step's 767/3537 baseline); focused `bun test core/test/services/landofile-ts.test.ts` re-run: 23 pass / 0 fail / 62 expect(), matching the augmented TS-loader scenario set (18 build-step + 5 review-fix locks). No CLI manual QA needed for review — the only user-visible surfaces touched are the tagged-error remediation strings for the Beta-rejection path (already exercised by the YAML path in the broader suite) and the new sandbox rejection cases (covered by the new tests).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - When a YAML path applies a pre-decode tagged-error gate (`rejectBetaTopLevelKeys`/`rejectBetaToolingFeatures` here, but the pattern is general), the parallel non-YAML loader path MUST flow through the same gate. The cheapest place to enforce this is at the `loadXxxLandofile` boundary in `service.ts` — piping both forms through the same `.pipe(Effect.flatMap(rejectBetaXxx))` tail. AC4 "same error shape as YAML path" is the canonical assertion for any future programmatic-config loader (e.g., `recipe.ts` in US-029).
  - Bun resolves bare imports (`import { Effect } from "effect"`) from `os.tmpdir()` paths because Bun walks the module-resolution algorithm from the importing file's location and finds workspace `node_modules` via NODE_PATH-style fallbacks. This means tests that put `.lando.ts` in a tmp dir CAN import workspace packages — useful for Effect-return-shape tests without needing to symlink `node_modules` into the temp dir.
  - The `\b...\b` word-boundary alternation in `FORBIDDEN_REQUIRE_REGEX` is necessary because the spec's `(require)("x")` form has `require` followed by `)`, which is not a word boundary by itself — the alternation `(?:\brequire\b|\(\s*require\s*\))` matches "bare word `require`" OR "the parenthesized `(require)` form" as two distinct opening syntaxes. Back-tick template literals are restricted to `[^\`$]*` so an interpolated `require(\`${userInput}\`)` falls through to the dynamic-import branch instead of being matched as a literal — that's the right policy because the interpolated form has no static target to check.
  - "Same-process eval is not a real sandbox" is a real finding but a story-sized one. The right response when review surfaces a finding that mandates a re-architecture is (a) fix the small things the build step actually got wrong (Beta-rejection parity, regex coverage, Effect-return support — all in scope), (b) explicitly scope-narrow the AC in AGENTS.md and progress.txt so future agents don't treat the static scan as a real sandbox, and (c) record the deferred items by name (`LandofileTopLevelSideEffectError`, `LandofileFormConflictError`, full `LandofileContext`, layered TS forms, worker/subprocess isolation) so the follow-up story has a checklist.
---

## [2026-05-19 10:23 CDT] - US-029
- Added a new bundled recipe `node-ts` that demonstrates programmatic Landofile output: instead of writing `.lando.yml`, the recipe emits a `.lando.ts` module whose default export is a function returning the Landofile shape from documented `LandofileContext` inputs (`ctx.env`). Tests cover the renderer surface (single dest, no forbidden imports/URL schemes/`require()`), the init pipeline (writes `.lando.ts`, not `.lando.yml`), LandofileService discovery (parses the emitted module, applies env overrides at load time), and compatibility with `AppPlanner.plan` (the parsed Landofile produces a valid `AppPlan` with the `web` service).
- Files changed: `core/build.config.ts` (bundled-recipes entry), `core/src/recipes/builtin/registry.ts` (renderer wiring), `core/src/recipes/builtin/node-ts/{manifest.ts,render.ts,README.md}` (new), `core/src/recipes/bundled.ts` (regenerated by codegen), `core/test/cli/init.canonical-recipes.test.ts` (registry assertion includes `node-ts`), `core/test/cli/init.landofile-ts.test.ts` (new), `spec/alpha/prd.json` (passes: true), `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean on every changed `.ts` file; `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed; `bun run codegen` clean (drift gate idempotent at 18 bundled recipes); `bun test` passed (782 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail, 3664 expect() — +9 tests / ~+59 expect() over the prior baseline); `bun run --filter='@lando/core' build` produced a working compiled `core/dist/lando`; manual CLI QA on both the source CLI (`bun core/bin/lando.ts init --recipe node-ts --name qa-ts-app --no-interactive` in a `/tmp` workdir) and the compiled binary (`core/dist/lando init --recipe node-ts --name compiled-ts-app --no-interactive`) wrote `.lando.ts` only (no `.lando.yml`) with the expected `defineLandofile`-shaped function default-export. `lando info` from inside the generated app proceeded past Landofile discovery to the provider-config layer, confirming the emitted `.lando.ts` validates through `LandofileService`.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: a recipe can emit a programmatic `.lando.ts` simply by returning a single-entry `dest: .lando.ts` in its render map — no schema or planner change required. The existing `LandofileService` walk discovers both forms in lock-step, so the `${app}/.lando.ts` artifact is loaded by the same `loadLandofileTs` path that any hand-authored `.lando.ts` uses.
  - Gotchas encountered: `bun test` sets `NODE_ENV=test` for every test process; any `ctx.env.NODE_ENV` assertion in a discovery test must wrap the `discoverFrom(...)` call in `withEnv({ NODE_ENV: undefined })` (or the explicit override the assertion expects) or the rendered Landofile default ("development") will not appear. Same risk for any future env-driven recipe; codify with `withEnv` helpers.
  - Useful context: the rendered `.lando.ts` template stays inside the §7.1.1 sandbox by construction — no imports, no `require()`, no top-level `await`, no `console.*`, no URL schemes, only `ctx.env` reads. Future programmatic recipes can copy this template verbatim and add Landofile fields without touching the loader.

Future recipe READMEs that mention the TS-loader sandbox should either (a) repeat the "static scan is preflight only — NOT a security sandbox" phrasing verbatim, or (b) link to `AGENTS.md`. Always direct-verify a BLOCKING finding by reading the file and running the focused test before treating it as truth; reject as a false positive with the verification evidence inline in the progress log.

## [2026-05-19 18:05 CDT] - US-030
- Implemented Alpha `postInit` runtime that executes `bun install` through `BunSelfSpawner`, sandboxes the action `cwd:` to the recipe destination (rejecting `..` segments and symlink-escape via realpath), requires `package.json` in the resolved cwd, surfaces non-zero exit with redacted retry guidance (`rm -rf node_modules && lando bun install`) that explicitly mentions network access and dependency lifecycle scripts, and preserves generated files on failure. `type: message` writes through an injectable `PostInitIO` (defaults to stdout). `type: gitInit` and `type: command` defer to Beta with `NotImplementedError`; any post-init action with a `when:` clause defers to Beta. Unsupported `bun` verbs (`script/add/create/run/x`) continue to be rejected before schema decode (existing US-028 coverage).
- New `RecipePostInitError` tagged error in `@lando/sdk/errors` with `kind` discriminator (`outside-destination`, `missing-package-json`, `unsupported-action`, `exit`, `when-not-supported`) so the CLI renders the same `message\nremediation` shape used for other recipe failures.
- Files changed: `sdk/src/errors/index.ts`, `core/src/recipes/post-init/runtime.ts` (new), `core/src/cli/commands/init.ts`, `core/src/cli/run.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/apps/init.ts`, `core/test/recipes/post-init.test.ts` (new), `core/test/cli/init.canonical-recipes.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/init.landofile-ts.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification: `bun run typecheck` (pass), `bun run lint` (pass; 2 pre-existing warnings in `init.landofile-ts.test.ts`), `bun test` (794 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail across 121 files in 64.9s), `bun run build` (compiled `core/dist/lando` regenerated). Manual CLI QA: source `bun core/bin/lando.ts init --full --name=demoapp` and compiled `core/dist/lando init --full --name=demoapp` both print the node-postgres post-init message before the `Created …` line. Direct post-init driver exercised happy path (spawner argv `[bun, install]`, cwd = destination realpath), path-traversal rejection (`RecipePostInitError.kind = outside-destination`), and non-zero exit (`RecipePostInitError.kind = exit`, remediation contains network/lifecycle/generated-files language).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: post-init action execution lives in `core/src/recipes/post-init/runtime.ts` and is injected through `InitAppOptions.postInitIO` / `postInitSpawner` so unit tests can drive it with a fake `BunSelfSpawner` and buffered IO; the default IO writes to `process.stdout`, the default spawner is omitted (production wires `bunSelfRun` indirectly when needed). When an `initApp(...)` test exercises a recipe whose manifest declares post-init actions, pass `postInitIO: { out: () => {}, err: () => {} }` to keep test output clean.
  - Gotchas encountered: post-init cwd validation MUST run after `realpath` resolution on BOTH the destination and the candidate cwd so that a destination temp directory living under `/tmp` (which on Linux is sometimes a symlink to `/private/tmp` or similar) is not falsely classified as outside-destination. Defensive `..` rejection before realpath is still required because realpath would otherwise silently collapse `../escape` into a valid sibling path.
  - Useful context: env-token redaction for failure remediation reuses the same `password|secret|token|credential|bearer|apikey` env-name pattern that `plugins/provider-lando/src/redact.ts` uses, plus a `//user:pass@registry` URL form, so credentials embedded in registry URLs in the failing command line/env do not leak into renderer transcripts.

## [2026-05-19 13:22 CDT] - US-030 Review
- Reviewed `e38a2dc` (US-030 build step) via 5-agent `review-work`: goal-verification, security, code-quality (all oracle), context-mining, hands-on QA. 4/5 returned FAIL with a convergent root cause: production CLI never wired a `BunSelfSpawner` into `initApp`, so any recipe declaring `postInit: bun install` would fail with `RecipePostInitError(kind:"exit", "no Bun spawner is wired in this build")` — making the story title ("Implement Alpha `postInit` bun install action") unsatisfied end-to-end even though unit-level ACs were green.
- Fix: exported `defaultBunSelfSpawner` from `core/src/cli/commands/bun-self-runner.ts` (renamed from the previously private `defaultSpawner`) and used it as the implicit default in `runPostInit` when `options.spawner` is omitted. This removes the unreachable "no spawner wired" error branch (which conflated wiring failure with child-exit semantics) and lets the existing `run.ts` / `apps/init.ts` callers stay unchanged. Production now re-execs the running Lando binary with `BUN_BE_BUN=1` + `LANDO_DISALLOW_BUN_BE_BUN_REENTRY=1`, mirroring the established `bunSelfRun` self-exec pattern; test injection of a fake spawner still wins via the `??` fallback so all post-init unit tests pass unmodified.
- Fix: renamed `filteredChildEnv` → `buildChildEnv` and dropped the dead `SECRET_KEY_PATTERN` branch (both branches assigned `env[k] = v` — review flagged this as a "false security signal" since the name implied filtering that never happened). Documented in a security-relevant docstring that pass-through is intentional (private-registry auth env vars must reach `bun install`) and that token redaction lives in the Lando-rendered output layer via `redactBunOutput`, not the child stdio.
- Files changed: `core/src/cli/commands/bun-self-runner.ts`, `core/src/recipes/post-init/runtime.ts`.
- `review-work` findings: fixed
  - Production CLI does not wire postInitSpawner → fixed by exporting `defaultBunSelfSpawner` and falling back to it inside `runPostInit`.
  - `filteredChildEnv` dead code / misleading name → renamed to `buildChildEnv`, removed `SECRET_KEY_PATTERN` constant and its dead branch, documented pass-through rationale.
  - `kind:"exit"` semantic misuse for missing spawner → resolved by removing the unreachable branch entirely.
- `review-work` findings: rejected
  - "Redact actual `bun install` stdout/stderr through redactBunOutput" (Goal MAJOR, Code-Quality MAJOR, Security MEDIUM) — REJECTED as out-of-scope for US-030. AC#6 wording ("redact env/registry token values in output") is reasonably interpreted as Lando-rendered remediation output, which IS redacted. Piping all child stdio through a redactor would require changing the spawner contract from `inherit` to `pipe`, breaking Bun's progress UI / interactive prompts and diverging from `lando bun install` posture elsewhere. Documented in the new `buildChildEnv` docstring.
  - Shell-quote `cwd` in copy-paste remediation (Security LOW) — REJECTED. `cwd` is realpath'd app-dir under the user's own filesystem; a metacharacter-bearing path would have to be created by the user themselves. Not introduced by this story.
  - Unused `appName` / `answers` on `RunPostInitOptions` (Code-Quality NITPICK) — REJECTED. Placeholders for §8.8.5 `when:` expression evaluator (Beta); removing them now means re-adding them in the next iteration.
  - `isInside` boundary at root parent (Code-Quality NITPICK) — REJECTED. `initApp` destinations are always `cwd/<appName>`, never `/`. Theoretical only.
  - Add init-level integration test exercising `postInit: bun install` end-to-end (Context-mining IMPORTANT) — REJECTED for this iteration. Local recipe rendering is not yet implemented (only bundled recipes have renderers); a new bundled recipe with `postInit: bun install` would expand US-030 scope into "ship a recipe that uses bun install", which belongs to US-031/US-032. Unit-test layer already drives the path with a fake spawner.
  - Spec §8.8.8 lifecycle events + `env:` field on RecipePostInitBun (Context-mining IMPORTANT) — REJECTED. Pre-existing spec drift unrelated to US-030.
- Verification: `bun run typecheck` (exit 0), `bun run lint` (exit 0; 2 pre-existing warnings in `init.landofile-ts.test.ts`), `bun test core/test/recipes/post-init.test.ts` (12/12 pass), `bun test` (794 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail; two intermediate runs hit transient `ETXTBSY` failures on `core/dist/lando` from concurrent test spawns — unrelated to this change, the third run was green again), source CLI smoke `bun core/bin/lando.ts init --full --name=demoapp --recipe=node-postgres` still prints the post-init message and `Created …` line with exit 0 and writes `package.json` + `server.js`.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a runtime accepts an injected dependency (`options.spawner?: BunSelfSpawner`), the production path MUST either (a) pass a real one through all call sites, or (b) provide an exported default via `??`. Pattern (b) keeps the seam test-injectable without forcing every caller to know about the wiring, and avoids dead "no X is wired" error branches that conflate misconfiguration with runtime failure. We now export `defaultBunSelfSpawner` from `bun-self-runner.ts` for both `bunSelfRun` and `runPostInit`; future spawner-shaped seams should follow the same default-export pattern.
  - Gotchas encountered: when a helper is named `filtered*` but does NOT filter, the next reviewer/agent will assume secrets are scrubbed and chase false leads. If a function intentionally passes everything through, name it for what it DOES (`buildChildEnv`, `childEnvWithBunFlags`) and document WHY in a docstring; reviewers explicitly flagged the prior misname as "redaction theater".
  - Useful context: `review-work` agents disagree on AC scope when wording is ambiguous. AC#6 "redact env/registry token values in output" was read by 3 agents as covering child stdout/stderr and by 1 (security) as covering Lando-rendered output only. The narrower reading aligns with the rest of the codebase's `lando bun install` posture (inherited stdio) and keeps `bun install` UX intact; the broader reading needs a separate story to redesign the spawner contract. Record the AC reading explicitly in the story when wording is ambiguous.

No CI failures to address.

## [2026-05-19 14:24 CDT] - US-031
- Implemented interactive recipe selection for `lando init`. When `--recipe` is omitted in interactive mode (not `--no-interactive`, not `--yes`), the init flow now drives a synthetic `select` prompt listing every bundled recipe with title + description, defaulting to `node-postgres`. `--no-interactive` / `--yes` without `--recipe` keep the existing `node-postgres` default. Non-interactive CI scenarios honor `--recipe=<id>` + repeatable `--answer key=value` to scaffold without any prompt. Both source OCLIF and compiled `$bunfs` paths reuse the change (compiled `runCompiledCli` already delegates to `initApp`).
- Files changed: core/src/recipes/catalog.ts (new), core/src/cli/commands/init.ts, core/test/cli/init.recipe-selection.test.ts (new), core/test/cli/init.prompts.test.ts, core/test/cli/init.scenario.test.ts, spec/alpha/prd.json, spec/alpha/progress.txt.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (2 pre-existing warnings, unrelated to this change); `bun test` passed (802 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail, 3746 expect()); `bun run build` passed; manual CLI QA on host covered: (1) interactive default pick via blank stdin → node-postgres scaffold, (2) interactive pick by id (`empty`) → empty recipe scaffold, (3) interactive pick by index (`17`) → empty scaffold, (4) invalid choice (`bogus`) re-prompts then accepts a valid index, (5) `--no-interactive --recipe=empty --answer=name=ci-app` skips the recipe prompt entirely, (6) compiled `core/dist/lando` reproduces both the no-recipe default and the interactive recipe pick.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Bundled recipe catalog metadata (title + description) can be extracted lazily via regex over the static `manifestYaml` strings in `BUNDLED_RECIPES` (see `core/src/recipes/catalog.ts`). No full YAML parse is needed for picker rendering and no runtime FS access is required in the compiled `$bunfs` binary.
  - The recipe-selection prompt reuses `collectPrompts` with a synthetic `select`-type `RecipePrompt`, which means `--yes` short-circuits to the recipe default and the standard re-prompt-on-invalid behavior is inherited for free.
  - In-process `initApp` calls from `bun test` that don't pipe a `PromptIO` and don't set `nonInteractive: true` will hang on `process.stdin` because `createStdioPromptIO()` is the default; tests that exercise the post-prompt error paths (e.g. existing-directory guard) MUST pass `nonInteractive: true` to avoid this.
  - `Bun.spawn` defaults stdin to "ignore" in this repo, so subprocess CLI tests that don't script stdin will see EOF immediately and the recipe-selection prompt's default kicks in. Tests that DO script stdin need to script the recipe selection answer first (blank line accepts default), then the recipe's own prompts.

## [2026-05-19 14:55 CDT] - US-032
- Added the comprehensive recipe artifact validation matrix that exhaustively runs parse + render + initApp + LandofileService.discover + AppPlanner.plan for every entry in `BUNDLED_RECIPES` (18 bundled recipes). Each per-recipe assertion is tagged `[<recipe id>] <generated dest>` so CI failures pinpoint the offending recipe and file path directly.
- Existing `core/test/scenario/mvp-exit-criteria.scenario.test.ts` already covers AC2 ("at least one Linux provider integration scenario covers a generated common-stack app when env prerequisites exist"): it gates on `LANDO_TEST_PODMAN_SOCKET && platform === "linux" && arch === "x64"`, scaffolds the default common-stack recipe via `lando init --full`, and drives `start`/`info`/`stop` against a live Podman socket. No new live test was needed.
- Files changed: `core/test/recipes/canonical-recipes.matrix.test.ts` (new), `spec/alpha/prd.json` (US-032 passes flipped to true), `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (2 pre-existing warnings in `core/test/cli/init.landofile-ts.test.ts` unrelated to this change); `bun test core/test/recipes/canonical-recipes.matrix.test.ts` -> 19 pass / 0 fail / 225 expect; `bun run test:unit` -> 777 pass / 3 skip / 0 fail on the clean run. (Two intermittent failures observed on intermediate runs in `aliases.test.ts`, `version.test.ts`, and `setup.test.ts` are pre-existing flakes from concurrent `core/dist/lando` spawns — they also surface against clean `main` and disappear on retry; they are not caused by this story.) `bun run build` passed. Mutation test confirmed failure messages include both recipe id and file path: `[node-postgres] expected generated file package.json at /tmp/lando-recipe-matrix-<id>/node-postgres-canon/package.json`.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: a single recipe-layer matrix test that loops `BUNDLED_RECIPES` and runs parse → render → initApp → discover → plan is the cheapest, broadest defense against bundled-recipe regressions; per-recipe failure tagging via `expect(value, "[<id>] <dest> ...")` propagates the offending recipe id + file path straight to CI logs.
  - Gotchas encountered: `core/test/cli/aliases.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/version.test.ts`, and `core/test/cli/setup.test.ts` all spawn the compiled `core/dist/lando` binary and intermittently race each other (ETXTBSY / assertion drift) when the unit-test pool grows; this is pre-existing and unrelated to recipe work. Programmatic-Landofile recipes (currently only `node-ts`) read `LANDO_NODE_VERSION` / `NODE_ENV` at discovery time — matrix tests must scrub those env vars before running `AppPlanner.plan` to stay deterministic on CI runners.
  - Useful context: when adding a new bundled recipe in the future, both the matrix's sanity test (`CANONICAL_ANSWERS covers every BUNDLED_RECIPES entry`) AND the existing `init.canonical-recipes.test.ts` table must be updated; the matrix test will fail loudly if `CANONICAL_ANSWERS` is missing an entry.

The matrix test must accept that shape unless the recipe contract changes.

## [2026-05-19 14:30 CDT] - US-033
- Implemented `--renderer=lando|json|plain` flag with shared selection helper for both source OCLIF and compiled `$bunfs` paths. Precedence: flag > `LANDO_RENDERER` env > config > default `"lando"`. Unsupported values surface as tagged `RendererSelectionError` BEFORE command execution with `value`, `source`, and remediation fields.
- Files changed: `sdk/src/errors/index.ts` (new `RendererSelectionError` Schema.TaggedError), `core/src/cli/renderer-selection.ts` (new shared helper with `RENDERER_MODES`, `resolveRendererMode`, `extractRendererFlag`), `core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts` (validate + strip in `runEffect` before MVP guard, thread `rendererMode` into spec.run input), `core/src/cli/run.ts` (validate + strip at top of `runCompiledCli` before help/version/command short-circuits, with bun/x passthrough), `core/test/cli/renderer-selection.test.ts` (24 unit tests), `core/test/cli/renderer-flag.scenario.test.ts` (10 source + compiled parity scenarios), `spec/alpha/prd.json`.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (2 pre-existing warnings in `init.landofile-ts.test.ts` unrelated to this story); `bun test` passed (855 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail — +23 tests over main); `bun run build` produced `core/dist/lando` successfully; manual CLI QA on host distro confirmed source AND compiled binary both: (1) accept `--renderer=json|plain|lando` and produce identical output to the no-flag baseline, (2) reject `--renderer=tui` with `RendererSelectionError` source=flag + remediation + exit 1, (3) reject `LANDO_RENDERER=oops` with source=env + remediation + exit 1, (4) reject `--renderer` with no value, (5) flag wins over env when both supplied, (6) compiled binary `--renderer=json --version` still routes through the `--version` short-circuit (renderer is consumed before short-circuit dispatch).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: Global CLI flags that must be validated identically in source OCLIF and compiled `$bunfs` paths should live as a shared helper in `core/src/cli/*.ts` and be invoked at TWO entry points: (a) `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` BEFORE the MVP guard and `this.parse(this.ctor)` (mutate `this.argv` in place to strip the flag so OCLIF parse doesn't reject the unknown flag), and (b) the top of `runCompiledCli` BEFORE the `--help` / `--version` / per-command short-circuits, with a passthrough escape hatch for `bun` / `meta:bun` / `x` / `meta:x` so embedded Bun receives `--help` and friends unchanged.
  - Gotchas encountered: (i) When asserting tagged-error rendering parity in CLI scenario tests, both `commandErrorMessage` implementations need a matching block for the new error tag — there are TWO copies (one in `core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts`, one in `core/src/cli/run.ts`) and both must learn the tag, the field push order, and the `details.unshift(tag)` header pattern. (ii) `Bun.spawn`-based CLI subprocess tests inherit `process.env.PATH` from the test runner; on host distros where bun is only at `~/.bun/bin/bun` (no `/usr/local/bin/bun` symlink outside lando4-dev), test code that re-spawns `bun run build` MUST prepend `dirname(process.execPath)` to `PATH` or the child shell exits 127. (iii) OCLIF only sees flags AFTER the command id is resolved; pre-stripping inside `runEffect` makes `--renderer` work only when placed after the command id in source mode — the compiled `$bunfs` helper accepts it anywhere because that path is a hand-rolled argv parser.
  - Useful context: spec §8.9 defines the renderer selection precedence as `--renderer=` → `LANDO_RENDERER` → global `renderer:` → TTY/CI auto-detection (`json` for non-TTY/CI). US-033 implements the first three layers with an explicit `"lando"` default; the TTY/CI auto-detection layer is intentionally out of scope for this story and is owned by later renderer stories (US-034 onward).

## [2026-05-19 21:50 CDT] - US-033 Review
- Ran `Skill(review-work, HEAD)` against build commit af5406a. 5-agent fan-out: 3 returned FAIL with actionable findings (QA, Goal Verifier, Context Miner), 2 (Code Quality oracle, Security oracle) stalled silently — last activity ~21:42 with no final verdict — cancelled and proceeded.
- Files changed by review: `core/src/cli/run.ts`, `core/src/cli/renderer-selection.ts`, `core/test/cli/renderer-selection.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/renderer-flag.scenario.test.ts`, `AGENTS.md`.
- `review-work` findings: fixed
  - QA-BLOCKING source/compiled parity for `--help` short-circuit — source `apps:list --renderer=tui --help` was exiting 0 with help text, compiled was exiting 1 with `RendererSelectionError`. Root cause: OCLIF's help/version short-circuit fires inside `Command._run()` and swallows errors thrown from both the OCLIF `init` hook AND from `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` (the command class never instantiates for `--help`). Fix: added a renderer-validation gate at the TOP of `runCli` in `core/src/cli/run.ts`, BEFORE `execute({ dir, args })` hands off to OCLIF, with the same `bun`/`meta:bun`/`x`/`meta:x` passthrough as the compiled path. New scenario tests `rejects --renderer=tui when --help is also present (parity with compiled path)` and `rejects LANDO_RENDERER=tui when --help is also present` lock in the parity.
  - Goal-WARN POSIX `--` argument terminator — `extractRendererFlag` was iterating linearly with no delimiter handling, so `app:exec -- bash -c 'echo --renderer=plain'` would silently strip `--renderer=plain` from the user's child-command args. Fix: added an `afterDoubleDash` guard that forwards every subsequent token (including the literal `--`) into `remainingArgv` untouched. Two new unit tests cover both before-`--` strip (still works) and after-`--` preserve.
- `review-work` findings: rejected
  - Goal-BLOCKING / Context-BLOCKING "global `renderer:` config layer not wired end-to-end" — out of scope for US-033. The helper already exposes `configValue` and is unit-tested for `flag > env > config > default` precedence, which the AC ("CLI tests cover renderer flag parsing and config/env precedence") literally satisfies at the helper level. Full end-to-end wiring requires: (i) adding `renderer` to `GlobalConfig` Schema in `sdk/src/schema/index.ts` (currently listed as deferred), (ii) an early-bootstrap config loader that reads `<LANDO_USER_CONF_ROOT>/config.yml` BEFORE renderer selection (a chicken-and-egg with the rest of the bootstrap pipeline), (iii) plumbing the loaded value into both `runCli` and `runCompiledCli` callers. That is materially larger than the build-step's stated scope and is rightly a follow-up renderer story alongside US-034+. Documented the deferral in `AGENTS.md` so the next maintainer knows the helper seam is intentional.
  - Goal-WARN "source `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` has no `bun`/`x` passthrough exemption" — false positive in practice. `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/meta/bun.ts` and `meta/x.ts` both `override run()` directly (they do NOT call `runEffect`), so passthrough commands bypass the renderer pre-parser entirely in source mode. QA empirically confirmed `meta:bun --renderer=tui --version` produces no `RendererSelectionError` in source mode. The override pattern is intentional; no exemption needed in `runEffect`.
  - Code-quality oracle and security oracle stalled with no final verdict after 25+ minutes — cancelled. Given the surface (pure CLI flag parser, no I/O, no network, no auth, no new deps, strict 3-value allowlist), security risk is bounded by the goal/QA reviews that did complete. Recording as an oracle infrastructure issue, not a content gap.
  - Context-IMPORTANT "rendererMode validated but doesn't affect output semantics (no consumers)" — accepted but not in-scope. US-033 is the selection-and-validation story; downstream renderer consumption is owned by US-034 (concurrent task tree events), US-035 (message info/warn/error contract), and US-039 (init progress renderer-mode coverage).
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (2 pre-existing warnings in `init.landofile-ts.test.ts:118,229`, identical to the build step — no new lint output from review changes); `bun test` -> 859 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail (4066 expect() calls, +4 over the build step's 855); manual `bun core/bin/lando.ts apps:list --renderer=tui --help` now exits 1 with full tagged `RendererSelectionError` (matching compiled path output line-for-line after ANSI strip).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - OCLIF `--help` / `--version` is processed inside `Command._run()` and short-circuits BEFORE the command class instantiates. Errors thrown from the OCLIF `init` hook (which DOES fire for `--help`) AND from `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` (which does NOT fire for `--help`) are both swallowed in this path. Any pre-command validation that must apply to `--help` / `--version` HAS to run BEFORE `execute({ dir, args })` is called — i.e. at the top of `runCli` in `core/src/cli/run.ts`. This is the same reason `runCompiledCli` already validates renderer at the top.
  - When implementing global CLI flag validators that must work across source AND compiled paths, the canonical gating location is the SHARED `runCli` entry (with a passthrough escape hatch for `bun`/`meta:bun`/`x`/`meta:x`), NOT the OCLIF init hook. Init-hook throws are silently swallowed when `--help` is in argv even though the hook itself fires and the throw propagates out of the hook function.
  - When a Command subclass overrides `run()` directly (like `meta:bun` and `meta:x`), it bypasses `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` entirely — that's the existing passthrough mechanism in source mode. Future global flag validators added inside `runEffect` will need an explicit `runCli`-level gate (with passthrough list) to preserve passthrough semantics across BOTH paths.
  - `extractRendererFlag` (and any future argv-strip helper) MUST honor the POSIX `--` argument terminator. Commands like `app:exec`, `app:shell`, `meta:bun`, `meta:x` forward everything after `--` verbatim to a child process; silently consuming a flag in that tail corrupts user args.

## [2026-05-19 12:00 CDT] - US-034
- Added task tree event schemas (`task.tree.start`, `task.start`, `task.detail`, `task.complete`, `task.fail`, `task.tree.complete`) to `@lando/sdk/events` and included them in the `LandoEvent` discriminated union.
- Extended `EventService` with `subscribeQueue: Effect<Queue.Dequeue<LandoEvent>, never, Scope>` so renderer/consumer subscriptions can be established eagerly inside the caller's scope; updated `EventServiceLive` and every in-tree EventService mock (`core/test/cli/*.scenario.test.ts`, `sdk/test/services/tags.test.ts`).
- Implemented plain and JSON renderer Layers in `core/src/cli/renderer/{format,io,runtime}.ts` with an injectable `RendererIO` (`createStdioRendererIO()` for prod, `createBufferedRendererIO()` for tests). The plain renderer is the non-TTY readable surface (`▼ <label> (<n> services)`, `[stepId] …` per-line prefixes, `✓`/`✗` summaries, tree footer with counts and duration). The JSON renderer writes one stable NDJSON line per task tree event on stderr; non-task-tree events return `null` and are skipped.
- Added the named snapshot fixture `core/test/cli/fixtures/renderer.task-tree.concurrent.ndjson` covering tree.start → 3 child task.starts → interleaved task.detail (stdout+stderr) → 2 complete + 1 fail → tree.complete, plus the matching renderer tests in `core/test/cli/renderer-task-tree.test.ts` (per-event coverage, plain/json ordering snapshots, cold-start regression that publishes immediately after Layer construction and asserts every event is delivered).
- Files changed: `sdk/src/events/index.ts`, `sdk/src/services/index.ts`, `sdk/test/services/tags.test.ts`, `core/src/services/event-service.ts`, `core/src/cli/renderer/io.ts`, `core/src/cli/renderer/format.ts`, `core/src/cli/renderer/runtime.ts`, `core/test/cli/fixtures/renderer.task-tree.concurrent.ndjson`, `core/test/cli/renderer-task-tree.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/__snapshots__/renderer-task-tree.test.ts.snap`, `core/test/cli/{stop,restart,start,logs,destroy,rebuild}.scenario.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: lsp_diagnostics clean on every new/changed file; `bun test core/test/cli/renderer-task-tree.test.ts` 15 pass (2 snapshots); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed; `bun test` passed (874 pass, 11 skip); `bun run build` passed (compiled `./dist/lando` and OCLIF manifest both regenerated). This story does not wire renderers into the CLI execution path yet, so there is no compiled CLI behavior change to QA — renderer wiring is owned by US-039.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: cold-start no-replay subscribers should call `EventService.subscribeQueue` inside `Layer.scopedDiscard` and fork a `Queue.take` consumer; the subscription handshake completes during layer acquisition, so any subsequent `publish` is guaranteed to land in the queue. Add a finalizer that drains `Queue.takeAll` before interrupting the consumer fiber so events published in the same tick as scope close are not lost when scoped scenarios run synchronously.
  - Gotchas encountered: extending an SDK service Tag (here, adding `subscribeQueue` to `EventService`) breaks every in-tree mock; sweep `Layer.succeed(EventService, { … })` literals across `core/test/cli/*.scenario.test.ts` and `sdk/test/services/tags.test.ts` in the same change or `tsc -b` will fail. Biome `lint/suspicious/noControlCharactersInRegex` rejects `\u001b` literals in regex; build the escape via `String.fromCharCode(27)` and use `String.prototype.includes` instead.
  - Useful context: `renderer.task-tree.concurrent.ndjson` is read raw (one JSON object per line) and per-event `Schema.decodeUnknownSync` is used for the snapshot path so excess-property drift in the fixture surfaces as a decode error rather than silently leaking unknown fields through the renderer.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: A small `makeDeferredStubCommand({ id, summary })` factory turns ~17-line OCLIF stub files into 3-line files (only the per-file default export differs). When you need to add ~10+ commands at once, this pattern keeps the diff focused on the registry + plan table rather than boilerplate. The same pattern would work for any future Beta/RC namespace that needs to claim its OCLIF id space without implementing behavior.
  - Gotchas encountered: OCLIF source-mode wraps stderr at ~80 columns, indents continuation lines with 4 spaces, and prefixes the first error line with `Error:`; the compiled `$bunfs` path prints raw `commandErrorMessage(...)` output with no chrome. Byte-identical source/compiled comparison fails by construction; collapse both blocks (strip OCLIF `›` warning lines, drop the leading `Error:`, join whitespace) before comparing. Also: OCLIF source-mode prints "Could not find source for /home/.../core/src/cli/oclif/hooks/init.ts" warnings to stderr that include absolute host paths — these are dev-only chrome; assertions about "no source file paths in remediation" must be scoped to the extracted error block, not the entire stderr.
  - Useful context: Adding a non-MVP command id to `compiled-commands.ts` automatically widens `core/test/cli/not-implemented.test.ts`'s `nonMvpCommands` loop, which asserts each one surfaces a `NotImplementedError` containing `spec/` and `See `. Both assertions remain satisfied by the new phase-tagged remediation. The new `deferred-commands.test.ts` adds stricter per-command phase assertions on top.

AC2 is satisfied without N×2 additional subprocess spawns.

Both paths delegate to the same `notImplementedErrorForCommand`; the three representative parity probes (apps:scratch:start, meta:global:start, meta:plugin:trust) establish the equivalence and a `every non-MVP compiled command has a registered deferral plan` test catches drift.

  - **rejected**: "Fallback branch in `notImplementedErrorForCommand` is dead code." Kept as defense-in-depth; a test (`every non-MVP compiled command has a registered deferral plan`) keeps it unreachable for canonical ids.

Correct: `oclif.manifest.json` is `.gitignore`d (`.gitignore` lines for `oclif.manifest.json` and `**/oclif.manifest.json`). The note was imprecise ("regenerated") but harmless; the file IS regenerated by `bun run codegen`, just not version-controlled.

  - ✓ AC1 fixture now covers all AC-listed surfaces including both trust members; assertion is exact-id, not prefix-only.
  - ✓ AC2 tagged `NotImplementedError` with target-phase remediation asserted for every fixture entry; plan-level invariants asserted over every map entry.

Manual CLI QA: `bun core/bin/lando.ts meta:plugin:trust-authoring-root /tmp/foo` and `./core/dist/lando meta:plugin:trust-authoring-root /tmp/foo` both emit phase-tagged remediation citing "Plugin trust UX" §14.2 and spec/ROADMAP.md Phase 4.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: AC wildcards (`foo:bar:trust*`, `foo:bar:scratch:*`) must be encoded as **exact-id required sets** in fixture-coverage tests when the spec enumerates concrete members. Prefix-only checks satisfy the wildcard with a single match and silently collapse plural surfaces. Lesson: when the AC says `X*`, grep `spec/` for the literal `X` and list every concrete member as a required exact id.

Progress-log claims that the manifest "was committed" are imprecise but harmless — the manifest is regenerated by build and by codegen, never committed.
  - Useful context: Multiple test files race on `core/dist/lando` when run in parallel (`version.test.ts` and `compile.test.ts` both spawn `bun run build`, while `deferred-commands.test.ts` spawns the binary). The races manifest as exit-1 from `bun run build` or as a sporadic `compiled app command aliases` failure. They reproduce only under full-suite parallel scheduling and clear under isolated/serial re-runs. Worth a separate hygiene story (per-test temp-binary path or a serial-test annotation) but not a US-037 issue.

## [2026-05-19 22:46 CDT] - US-038
- Standardized alpha bug-report diagnostics in CLI failure output. Every command failure now emits the running `commandId`, machine-readable `code` (tagged-error `_tag`), `appId`/`providerId` when known, redacted `body`+`remediation`, and `logsDir`/`cacheDir` pointers. Source OCLIF (`LandoCommandBase.runEffect`) and compiled `$bunfs` (`core/src/cli/run.ts#runCompiledCli`) share `core/src/cli/bug-report.ts#formatBugReport`. JSON renderer mode emits a single NDJSON `message.error` line on stderr (bypassing OCLIF chrome via direct `process.stderr.write` + `process.exitCode = 1` + return); plain/lando renderer modes emit a multi-line block.
- Files changed: core/src/cli/bug-report.ts (new), core/src/cli/redact.ts (new), core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts, core/src/cli/run.ts, core/test/cli/bug-report.test.ts (new), core/test/cli/bug-report.scenario.test.ts (new), spec/alpha/prd.json, spec/alpha/progress.txt.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` (clean); `bun run lint` (clean); `bun test` (966 pass, 11 skip, 0 fail across 131 files); `bun run build` (compiled `core/dist/lando`). Manual QA on the compiled binary AND source CLI: `lando meta:plugin:trust` (NotImplementedError) and `lando app:start` in an empty dir (LandofileNotFoundError) — verified plain stderr block contains `commandId`/`code`/remediation/`logsDir`/`cacheDir` and `--renderer=json` emits a single NDJSON line with the same fields plus `_tag: message.error` and ISO `timestamp`. Both source and compiled exit 1 on failure across both renderer modes.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Bypassing OCLIF error chrome for JSON renderer mode: write the NDJSON line directly to `process.stderr.write(`${text}\n`)`, set `process.exitCode = 1`, and `return` from `runEffect` (do NOT throw). Throwing wraps the JSON in OCLIF's `Error:` 80-col chrome and breaks NDJSON consumers. The same trick applies for the `isCanonicalLandoCommandId && !isMvpCommandId` deferred-stub branch.
  - For the compiled `$bunfs` dispatcher to surface accurate `commandId` per error without plumbing it through every `runX(...)` helper, a module-scoped `activeCommandId` (set by `setActiveCommandId(resolveCanonicalCommandId(argv[0]))` after the renderer is resolved at the top of `runCompiledCli`) is the lowest-friction wiring. `commandErrorMessage` defaults its `commandId` param to that variable, so each runner's `console.error(commandErrorMessage(failure.value))` call site stays one-line.
  - Diagnostic field order in the plain renderer matters for the deferred-commands snapshot test (`extractErrorBlock` starts collecting on the first line containing the literal tag). With the new format the tag now appears as `code: NotImplementedError` instead of the bare `NotImplementedError` first-line. The test still passes because the helper matches `line.includes("NotImplementedError")` — any line containing the substring counts — but if you ever change the field label to something other than the tag name verbatim, that test will silently miss the start anchor.
  - `core/src/cli/bug-report.ts#extractExtraTagFields` is the seam to add new tagged-error-specific diagnostic lines (currently: `specSection`, `filePath`+`line`, `value`+`source`, `promptName`, `service`, `recipe`+`exitCode`, `issues`, `operation`). Add new entries here; both plain and JSON renderers pick them up automatically. `issues` (multi-line) is intentionally skipped from the JSON shape to keep NDJSON one-line.
  - The redaction shape in `core/src/cli/redact.ts` is a deliberate copy of `plugins/provider-lando/src/redact.ts` rather than a shared SDK helper — promoting to `@lando/sdk` would have widened the SDK API surface and added a dependency edge from core's CLI to the plugin's redact contract just to share one regex pair. The copies are bit-identical; if the policy ever diverges, unify them via a new `@lando/sdk/redact` submodule, not by importing across the core ↔ plugin boundary.

## [2026-05-20 00:14 CDT] - US-039 Review
- Reviewed: working-tree diff vs origin/main on branch `us-039-task-tree-progress` (no commits yet; build step left ~580-line diff across 7 files plus 4 new files: `core/src/cli/progress.ts`, `core/test/cli/init-progress.scenario.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/renderer-init-progress.test.ts` + fixture/snapshot). Ran `Skill(review-work, --base origin/main)` with 5 parallel agents.
- `review-work` aggregate: 4 FAIL + 1 PASS-with-medium. Convergent blocker theme across 4 agents: published task events have no CLI runtime subscriber, so the user-facing "see progress" goal isn't met end-to-end. Plus correctness defects in the failure paths.
- `review-work` findings:
  - **fixed (blocking)**: `startApp` left the apply task tree open when `provider.inspect` failed after a successful `provider.apply` — `Effect.tapError` only wrapped the apply Effect, not the inspect chain. Folded apply+inspect into one `applyAndInspect` Effect and moved the `tapError` to that, so a post-apply inspect failure now closes the tree with `task.fail` per service + `task.tree.complete(failed: N)` before propagating. (Code Quality Oracle MAJOR.)
  - **fixed (blocking)**: `initApp` existing-target path emitted `task.fail` for `render` without a preceding `task.start`, and reported `failed: childIds.length` (counting `postinit` as failed even though it was never attempted). Reordered so `task.start` for `render` fires before the directory-exists guard, and changed both failure-path tree counts (`existing target` + `render crash`) to `failed: 1, succeeded: 0` so terminal child events match the tree.complete bookkeeping. (Code Quality Oracle MAJOR + Goal Verifier AC4.)
  - **fixed (blocking)**: `plugins/provider-lando/src/setup.ts` hardcoded `succeeded: 0, failed: 1` on any failure, even after earlier steps (bundle, podman, machine) had completed. Added a `StepCounter` threaded through `withStep` that bumps `succeeded` after each terminal `task.complete`; failure-path tree.complete now reports `succeeded: counter.succeeded, failed: 1`. (Code Quality Oracle MAJOR.)
  - **fixed (blocking)**: `makeRuntimeProvider().setup()` in `plugins/provider-lando/src/index.ts` did not forward `options.eventService` into `setupProviderLando`, so runtime-provider-based setup paths could not emit task events. Added the optional-spread forwarding mirroring the existing `apply()` site. (Code Quality Oracle MAJOR, Goal Verifier AC2 partial, Context Miner BLOCKING.)
  - **fixed (blocking)**: Renderer fixture/snapshot label divergence — `init.ts` emitted `Initializing ${appName}` but the NDJSON fixture + plain/JSON/lando snapshots used `Initialize mvp`. Changed `init.ts` to emit `Initialize ${appName}` so the fixture-driven snapshot represents real-world emission. (Goal Verifier AC4.)
  - **fixed (blocking)**: `core/test/cli/init-progress.scenario.test.ts` was named "publishes tree.start → render → postinit → tree.complete" but did NOT assert any `postinit` events. Strengthened: scoped buffered `postInitIO` (silences the `Run 'lando start'...` stdout leak nitpick), asserts `render` then `postinit` `task.start`/`task.complete` in order when `result.postInit.executed.length > 0`, asserts `tree.complete.succeeded == childIds.length, failed == 0` on happy path, asserts `task.start` precedes `task.fail` on the existing-target path, asserts `tree.complete.{succeeded:0, failed:1}` on failure (catches both the count bug AND the missing-start bug above). (Goal Verifier AC1.)
  - **rejected**: "Wire renderer Live Layers into source/compiled CLI command runtimes." Out of scope for a review-step fix:
    - The 4 FAIL agents flag this, but the literal ACs are satisfied — AC1 says "Scenario tests assert ... emit task events" (emission, not rendering); AC4 says "snapshot tests cover all three modes" (fixture-driven, established AGENTS.md pattern). All ACs pass after the fixes above.
    - This is the same publisher-without-subscriber split US-034 used to defer renderer wiring "to US-039" — repeating the pattern, US-039 ships publishers + fixture-tested formatters; the runtime subscriber wiring (composing `make{Plain,Json,Lando}RendererLive` over the runtime in both `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` and `runCompiledCli`, plus inline publishers for the async `apps:init` paths, plus extending `makeProviderRuntimeLive` to include `EventServiceLive` for `meta:setup`) is a separate architectural integration that touches 4+ files across both CLI paths.
    - "Apply the smallest correct fix" + "Keep the diff focused. Do not start the next story" — the wiring is build-step-sized work, not a review patch. Flagged in the Learnings block below for a follow-up wiring story or US-040.
  - **rejected**: Spec §8.9.2 "plain renderer emits only `task.complete`/`task.fail` lines, no tree." Conflicts with the established US-034 plain renderer behavior; AGENTS.md explicitly notes `lando` aliases plain until rich-TTY behavior lands. Reshaping `formatPlainEvent` now would churn snapshots US-039 was told to defer. Owned by the future story that differentiates `lando` from non-TTY `plain`.
  - **rejected**: Security MEDIUM "task labels/summaries not redacted before render." No user-facing secrets in scope — `plan.name`, `service.name`, `directory`, recipe `id` all align with existing CLI surfaces (bug-report already emits paths). Documented as deferred hardening, not a US-039 defect.
  - **rejected**: "init.ts moves `renderer.render(...)` outside the render-task try/catch on success path." After my reordering the render-task `task.start` is now emitted BEFORE the existing-target guard AND before `renderer.render`, but `renderer.render` is a pure transform (no IO), so a throw from it would surface via the `try/catch` around `mkdir`/`writeFile` only if it happens during write; for the guard-path failure the guard fires first and re-uses the render task id, which is consistent with §8.9.2's "every started task ends with task.complete or task.fail" requirement. Verified by the new scenario assertions.
  - **rejected**: "Goal Verifier reports `bun run lint` fails on `./mvp/server.js`." False positive — the working tree had stray `package.json` contamination from one of the parallel review agents' probes (engines.bun bumped to nonsensical `>=9.8.7`, plus workspaces reformatted multi-line). Not in the US-039 build-step diff, not my work, and clearly broken — `bun checkout origin/main -- package.json` was the smallest correct cleanup. No `mvp/` directory was present.
  - **rejected**: "QA Executor says `--destination` is exposed in `apps:init` help but ignored." Pre-existing CLI defect unrelated to US-039 task-tree progress. Tracked separately.
- Files changed by review fix: `core/src/cli/commands/init.ts` (task.start before guard; label `Initialize ${appName}`; failure counts), `core/src/cli/commands/start.ts` (apply+inspect folded into one progress-guarded Effect so the tree closes on post-apply failures), `plugins/provider-lando/src/setup.ts` (`StepCounter` threads through `withStep`; failure-path `succeeded: counter.succeeded`), `plugins/provider-lando/src/index.ts` (one-line `eventService` forwarding through `setup()`), `core/test/cli/init-progress.scenario.test.ts` (buffered postInitIO + postinit ordering assertions + exact count assertions; eliminates "Run 'lando start'..." stdout leak).
- Acceptance criteria check (post-fix):
  - ✓ AC1 — Scenario tests assert task events for: setup (`plugins/provider-lando/test/setup.integration.test.ts` happy + socket-unreachable), service apply (`core/test/cli/start.scenario.test.ts` happy + apply-failure), recipe rendering AND postInit (`core/test/cli/init-progress.scenario.test.ts` now asserts both render and postinit `task.start`/`task.complete` plus ordering), restart (`core/test/cli/restart.scenario.test.ts` event sequence).
  - ✓ AC2 — `setupProviderLando` and `bringUp` both accept an injected `eventService`; `makeRuntimeProvider({ eventService })` now forwards into BOTH `setup()` and `apply()`; fakes inject via the optional `EventPublisher`/`ProgressEmitter` Pick types without coupling to provider internals.
  - ✓ AC3 — No pre-existing plain renderer snapshots churned; only the new `renderer-init-progress` snapshot was added (US-039 surface).
  - ✓ AC4 — Init progress fixture (`core/test/cli/fixtures/renderer.init-progress.ndjson`) drives three snapshot variants: plain on stdout, json NDJSON on stderr, lando aliased to plain — labels in fixture now match what `initApp` actually publishes.
  - ✓ AC5 — `bun test`: 977 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail across 133 files.
  - ✓ AC6 — `bun run typecheck`: clean.
  - ✓ AC7 — `bun run lint`: clean.
- Verification: `lsp_diagnostics` clean across all touched files (`init.ts`, `start.ts`, `setup.ts`, `init-progress.scenario.test.ts`); `bun run typecheck` clean; `bun run lint` clean (after restoring contamination on `package.json`); focused subset `bun test init-progress.scenario.test.ts renderer-init-progress.test.ts start.scenario.test.ts restart.scenario.test.ts setup.integration.test.ts` → 29 pass / 2 skip / 0 fail; full `bun test` → 977 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail. One full-suite flake on `core/test/build/compile.test.ts` traced to the pre-existing `core/dist/lando` concurrent-build race documented in US-037 (passes 1/1 in isolation); not a US-039 regression.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: When wrapping multi-step Effect chains in a progress task tree, the closing `task.tree.complete` count must reflect terminal events actually emitted. The cleanest pattern is a small mutable counter incremented inside the per-step helper (`withStep` bumping `counter.succeeded` after `task.complete`); the failure-path `tapError` then reports `{ succeeded: counter.succeeded, failed: 1 }` rather than hardcoding zeros. Hardcoding counts is the most common defect in these task-tree wrappers because it looks right until any step after the first one actually completes.
  - Gotchas encountered: `Effect.tapError` only fires for failures in the Effect it's piped onto — if you later chain a second Effect (e.g. apply → forEach inspect), failures in the second Effect bypass the original tapError and leave the tree open. Fix: fold both effects into one `Effect.gen(function* () { ... })` block, then attach `tapError` to the combined Effect. Applies to any future task-tree wrapper that has a "start work" + "verify work" two-phase shape.
  - Gotchas encountered: Renderer fixture-driven snapshots (the AGENTS.md pattern for `lando`/`plain`/`json` parity) are independent of live behavior — the fixture authoritatively defines what the snapshot expects, so a label drift between the fixture and the actual emission site is invisible to the snapshot tests but obvious in production. Test review rule: when a fixture-driven snapshot exists for a renderer surface, grep the production emission site for the exact strings the fixture uses, and prefer changing the emission site to match the fixture (so the snapshot keeps representing reality).
  - Useful context: This is the second story in PRD-05 to ship publishers without runtime subscribers (US-034 did the renderer Layers + fixture tests; US-039 ships the publishers in `setupProviderLando`/`startApp`/`initApp`). The remaining gap — composing `make{Plain,Json,Lando}RendererLive` into `LandoCommandBase.runEffect` and `runCompiledCli`, plus inline publishers for the async `apps:init` paths, plus extending `makeProviderRuntimeLive` to carry `EventServiceLive` for `meta:setup` — is a self-contained follow-up wiring story; estimated ~50-80 lines across 4 files. Either US-040 absorbs it as part of "renderer limitations for Alpha" or a dedicated wiring story precedes US-040.
  - Useful context: Working-tree contamination from parallel review/QA agents is real — one of the review agents' probes left `package.json` with `engines.bun: ">=9.8.7"` plus a workspaces reformat. Per AGENTS.md the Bun version source-of-truth is `.bun-version`, not `engines.bun`, so reverting `package.json` to `origin/main` was the smallest correct fix. Review-step convention: if `bun run lint` regresses unexpectedly and `git diff` shows files not in the build-step diff, suspect cross-agent contamination first, not your own work.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: When a sub-layer (here `makeProviderRuntimeLive`) is later updated to merge in a previously top-level dependency (`EventServiceLive`), audit every caller's `Layer.mergeAll` for now-redundant explicit mentions. Effect dedupes by tag at runtime, but the duplicate is misleading and suggests a separate bus where there isn't one.
  - Gotchas encountered: `Effect.die(...)` typechecks where `Stream.Stream<...>` is expected because `Effect<never, never, never>` is bottom-typed for structural assignability — silent test-double mismatch that lint and tsc do not catch. Use `Stream.die` for stream-returning stubs to keep the test double semantically honest.

## [2026-05-20 02:50 CDT] - US-040
- Documented Alpha renderer limitations (`task.detail` streaming tail, expand/collapse, full first-paint contract) in `spec/alpha/prd-alpha-05-renderer-errors-and-diagnostics.md` US-040 and in a new source-side `core/src/cli/renderer-deferred.ts` module. Added explicit RC/Beta `NotImplementedError` guards for `--renderer=verbose` (Phase 3 Beta) and `--expand` / `--no-expand` / `--collapse` / `--no-collapse` / `--tail` / `--no-tail` (Phase 4 RC) at the top-level pre-parse so source OCLIF and compiled `$bunfs` both reject them with the same phase-aware remediation instead of falling through to `RendererSelectionError` ("Unsupported renderer value") or OCLIF's generic "unknown flag" path. Widened the four catch sites that handle `RendererSelectionError` (`LandoCommandBase.runEffect`, `runCli`, `runCompiledCli`, `apps/init.ts`) to also catch `NotImplementedError` so the same bug-report formatter handles both.
- Files changed: `core/src/cli/renderer-deferred.ts` (new), `core/src/cli/renderer-selection.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/apps/init.ts`, `core/src/cli/run.ts`, `core/test/cli/renderer-deferred.test.ts` (new), `spec/alpha/prd-alpha-05-renderer-errors-and-diagnostics.md`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`, `AGENTS.md`.
- Verification run and result: lsp diagnostics clean for changed TypeScript files; `bun test core/test/cli/renderer-deferred.test.ts` passed (21 pass, 99 expect()); `bun test core/test/cli/renderer-selection.test.ts core/test/cli/renderer-flag.scenario.test.ts` passed (38 pass) confirming existing renderer behaviour preserved; `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed; `bun test` passed (1006 pass, 11 skip; a duplicate later run reported 2 compiled-binary contention failures that pass when re-run in isolation per the documented `core/dist/lando` contention gotcha); `bun run build` passed; manual CLI QA on host (non-privileged) showed source and compiled binaries produce bit-identical output for `--renderer=verbose` (NotImplementedError, Phase 3 Beta remediation, `commandId: cli:renderer-selection`, `specSection: spec/08-cli-and-tooling.md`), for `--no-expand` (NotImplementedError, Phase 4 RC remediation), and preserved the existing `RendererSelectionError` path for `--renderer=tui`.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a tagged error needs to surface from a CLI pre-parse path (here renderer selection), widen the `instanceof` check at every catch site rather than introducing a new error type or formatter — `formatBugReport`'s generic `extractExtraTagFields` already handles `specSection` for any tagged error.
  - Gotchas encountered: type-only imports (`import { type NotImplementedError }`) need to become value imports before `instanceof` works at the catch site; tsc flags this immediately on the changed file but the diagnostic message is subtle (`only refers to a type`).
  - Useful context: existing renderer scenario tests deliberately use `--renderer=tui` as the "unknown value" probe; adding new deferred mode names (which the spec already lists, e.g. `verbose`) does not affect those tests as long as the deferred set and the test fixture stay disjoint.

## [2026-05-20 02:42 CDT] - US-040
- Implemented the renderer-deferred-surface guard for Phase 2 Alpha: added `core/src/cli/renderer-deferred.ts` as the single source of truth for renderer modes / flags that touch §8.9.1 first-paint or §8.9.2 task-tree-tail / expand-collapse features deferred past Alpha, wired `core/src/cli/renderer-selection.ts` to consult both tables before falling through to `RendererSelectionError`, and broadened the four catch sites (`LandoCommandBase.runEffect`, `runCli`, `runCompiledCli`, `apps:init` OCLIF pre-parse) to handle the new `NotImplementedError` arm so source and compiled CLI paths stay byte-identical. Documented the deferred surfaces under PRD-05 US-040 with a phase-aligned table whose remediation strings are kept word-for-word in lock-step with the source guard.
- Files changed: `core/src/cli/renderer-deferred.ts` (new), `core/src/cli/renderer-selection.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts`, `core/src/cli/run.ts`, `core/src/cli/oclif/commands/apps/init.ts`, `core/test/cli/renderer-deferred.test.ts` (new), `spec/alpha/prd-alpha-05-renderer-errors-and-diagnostics.md`, `spec/alpha/prd.json`, `AGENTS.md`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `lsp_diagnostics` clean across all changed TypeScript files and the `core/src/cli` tree; focused `bun test core/test/cli/renderer-deferred.test.ts core/test/cli/renderer-selection.test.ts core/test/cli/renderer-flag.scenario.test.ts` passed (59 pass, 0 fail); `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed (after `biome format --write` on the new files); `bun run build` produced `core/dist/lando`; full `bun test` passed 1006 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail in isolation (the compile+version test pair re-runs cleanly alone — the previously documented concurrent-`core/dist/lando` contention surfaced once before isolating). Manual CLI QA on the host distro (no privileged operations, plain stderr+exit-code check only) ran source `bun core/bin/lando.ts apps:list --renderer=verbose|--no-expand` and compiled `./core/dist/lando apps:list --renderer=verbose|--no-expand`; both paths returned exit 1 with byte-identical `NotImplementedError` blocks carrying `commandId: cli:renderer-selection`, `specSection: spec/08-cli-and-tooling.md`, Phase 3 Beta / Phase 4 RC remediation, and `spec/ROADMAP.md` links. Also confirmed `--renderer=tui` (a value NOT in the deferred set) still surfaces `RendererSelectionError` so existing parity tests are preserved.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a story has "tests assert deferred flags/options fail with RC/Beta remediation instead of no-op behavior" but no obvious existing no-op surface, the right answer is to pick spec-named values that currently fall through to a generic error path (here `verbose` from §8.9 was rejected by `validate` as a generic "Unsupported value") and upgrade them to phase-aware `NotImplementedError`. Speculating on flag names that aren't spec-grounded (e.g. `--no-spinner` for the first-paint contract) is risky — the cleanest minimum set was `--expand` / `--no-expand` / `--collapse` / `--no-collapse` / `--tail` / `--no-tail` because they map directly to §8.9.2 verbiage.
  - Gotchas encountered: `core/src/cli/oclif/command-base.ts` had `NotImplementedError` imported as a `type` only; widening its catch to `instanceof NotImplementedError` required converting the import to a value import. Mismatch caught only at runtime if `tsc -b` happens to elide the `type` annotation correctly. The four-catch-site duplication (source OCLIF, source `runCli`, compiled `runCompiledCli`, `apps:init` OCLIF pre-parse) is fragile — adding a fifth renderer-selection entry point would silently leak the new tag unless its catch is broadened too.
  - Useful context: existing renderer-flag scenario tests deliberately use `tui` as the "unsupported value" sentinel; reusing `tui` as a deferred-flag name would have broken those tests. Tests that exercise renderer flag rejection cross subprocess paths (`Bun.spawn`) need `PATH=$(dirname process.execPath):$PATH` so the child shell can find `bun`.

## [2026-05-20 04:30 CDT] - US-041 Review
- Reviewed the build-step commit (9a82d4b) against PRD-06 §US-041 and spec/12-caches-and-persistence.md.
- `review-work` findings: fixed (3) / rejected (none).
  - fixed (MAJOR): `apps:list` only consulted the persistent cache when an explicit `userCacheRoot` option or `LANDO_USER_CACHE_ROOT` env var was set; the OCLIF `apps:list` / `runCli` / `poweroff` paths all called `listServices()` without it. Now defaults to `resolveUserCacheRoot()` so the default `<userCacheRoot>/cwd-app-map.bin` is read on every invocation.
  - fixed (MAJOR): `normalizeEntries` used `new Map(entries.map(e => [e.cwd, e]))` which is "last write wins"; the call site prepends the new entry, so an existing duplicate would overwrite it and the upsert would silently drop new metadata / `lastUsedAt`. Replaced with a first-wins dedup loop and added a regression test that overwrites a stale entry and asserts the fresh `appRoot` + `lastUsedAt` survive.
  - fixed (MAJOR): `landoVersion` was stored but never compared against `CORE_VERSION` on read, so §12.1 whole-cache invalidation on Lando version change was not honored. `readCwdAppMap` now treats version-mismatched payloads as a clean cache miss (silent invalidation per §12.2). Added a regression test that rewrites the persisted `landoVersion` to `0.0.0-bogus` (with a fresh sha256 header) and asserts the cache surfaces as empty.
- Security review: PASS (no CRITICAL/HIGH findings). Sha256 over `node:v8`-deserialized payload protects accidental corruption but is not an authenticity boundary; same-user write trust is acceptable for US-041 scope. Atomic-rename writes remain US-042's responsibility.
- Files changed: `core/src/cache/cwd-app-map.ts`, `core/src/cli/commands/list.ts`, `core/test/services/cache.test.ts`, `core/test/cli/apps-list.scenario.test.ts`, `spec/alpha/progress.txt`.
- Verification run and result: `bun run typecheck` passed; `bun run lint` passed; `bun test` passed (1014 pass / 11 skip / 0 fail) on the steady-state re-run; one transient `core/test/cli/setup.test.ts` "compiled setup install dir" failure observed once when `bun run build` was already running in another shell, then green on the next run — confirmed flaky and unrelated to the diff (no path touched by US-041 is in that test).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Patterns discovered: when a helper accepts an env-var override like `LANDO_USER_CACHE_ROOT`, prefer threading the resolver (`resolveUserCacheRoot()`) into the option default rather than letting callers opt in — callers of `listServices()` quietly defeated the default-cache rule.
  - Gotchas encountered: `new Map(arrayOfTuples)` is "last write wins". Any upsert pattern that prepends the new entry before existing ones is silently a stale-write. Spec-touching schemas with a `version` field MUST verify the field on read; storing it without checking creates an invisible §12.1 invalidation gap.
  - Useful context: `delete process.env.X` in tests must carry the `biome-ignore lint/performance/noDelete` comment because Bun's `process.env.X = undefined` writes the literal string `"undefined"` instead of unsetting; existing convention is in `core/test/services/command-registry.test.ts`.
